New French Cabinet Implements Social Policies Prime Minister Blum Announces Guiding Principles Domestic Affairs to Protect Workers' Interests Diplomacy to Complete Collective Security 32

(Paris) Prime Minister Blum presented a bill to the parliament today, approving the demands of 600,000 striking workers nationwide, similar in nature to the American "New Deal." (National Telegram, 6th)

(Paris) Prime Minister Blum announced the new government's policy guidelines in the Chamber of Deputies today. All legislation will have a strong socialist character, and he urged the parliament to pass it before the summer recess, after which detailed regulations will be announced by order. The Radical Party held a meeting this morning and unanimously decided to support Blum's policy guidelines, so Blum will surely obtain a majority in the Chamber of Deputies. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

(Paris) The declaration of the cabinet's policy guidelines, typed on seven pages, is summarized as follows:

"Regarding domestic affairs, the cabinet has decided to act quickly to initiate reforms in both spirit and substance, in order to meet the expectations of the entire nation. It will prepare and submit legal bills to both houses of parliament next week, requesting their immediate consideration and vote. These legal bills are divided into: amnesty for political prisoners; implementation of a 40-hour work week; allowing trade unions to represent workers and sign labor contracts with employers; one week of paid annual leave for workers; a large-scale public works program; nationalization of military industries; reorganization of the Banque de France; and amendment of certain legal decrees."

In addition, the entire tax system will also be revised to allow production and commerce to intensify work and the economy to recover. "In short, the cabinet has decided to restore and preserve the true republican spirit in all administrative organs."

As for the state of national finances, Finance Minister Auriol will report the true economic and financial situation to the nation within a few days.

Regarding diplomacy, the French nation will work together with all countries in the world for peace. "For peace, and respect for international law and international treaties, and the fulfillment of promises, are mutually beneficial. It is hoped that after the collective security mechanism is organized, all countries in the world can end the arms race." (Havas dispatch, 6th)

(Paris) Prime Minister Blum read the declaration of the cabinet's policy guidelines in the Chamber of Deputies this afternoon, while Associate Prime Minister Daladier read it in the Senate. Both houses were packed with people. Left-wing members of parliament frequently applauded, while right-wing members listened intently. When the Prime Minister declared in the Lower House that military industries should be nationalized, the right-wing members of parliament showed slight signs of agitation, and the left-wing members of parliament immediately shouted, "Arms merchants, shut your mouths! Defeated generals, shut your mouths!" The Senate meeting was very quiet. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

President of the Banque de France Replaced 33

Another Large Outflow of Gold

(Paris) The cabinet held a State Council meeting this morning and decided to appoint Rabier, President of the Court of Audit, as the President of the Banque de France, and to appoint the incumbent President, Tannery, as Honorary President. Rabier is one of France's most famous financial experts and a long-time friend of Prime Minister Léon Blum. His appointment as President of the Banque de France had been anticipated by financial circles two weeks ago and was not considered surprising. The State Council then approved the declaration of the cabinet's policy guidelines, which Prime Minister Léon Blum and Associate Prime Minister Daladier will read simultaneously in the Chamber of Deputies and the Senate this afternoon. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

(Paris) The new French government has encountered thorny issues of strikes and gold outflows from the start. Today, gold worth 320 million francs was shipped to New York on the steamer Deutschland. In total, gold worth $125 million has been shipped to the United States in the past six weeks, causing the devaluation of the franc to be discussed again. The government is now working hard to resolve the labor unrest. The number of striking workers has now exceeded 500,000. After meeting with cabinet members for two hours, Prime Minister Blum issued a statement saying that the government is determined to do its utmost to promote a satisfactory resolution of the strike. The cabinet also passed the new government's policy statement today, which will be submitted to parliament for a vote on Saturday. (National Telegram, 5th)

(Washington) The London Exchange News reported that Britain and the United States had informally agreed that the two countries should take joint action when France abandons the gold standard. U.S. Treasury Department officials do not believe this statement. Although the authorities have remained silent on the matter, one official stated that if Britain and the United States had agreed on a joint action plan, then Treasury Secretary Morgenthau would have announced it. (Reuters dispatch, 5th)

(London) Although there is still a strong undercurrent of panic in the foreign exchange market, today the pressure on gold coins has eased, and traders' minds have been slightly calmed. However, the position of the franc has not improved. Speculators are taking a resolute wait-and-see attitude because they believe that the French government will implement severe monetary regulations and will not immediately lower the value of the currency. Furthermore, it is generally believed that the initial large-scale sale of francs due to labor unrest is now coming to an end. Everyone will pay attention to the efforts of the new French Minister of the Interior, Salengro, to peacefully resolve labor disputes. The broadcast speech given by French Prime Minister Blum is generally regarded as lacking constructive elements. (Reuters dispatch, 5th)

French Labor Unrest May Be Resolved 34

Securities All Show Improvement

(Paris) New Prime Minister Léon Blum, Minister of the Interior Salengro, Minister of National Economy Spinasse, and Minister of Labor Lebas met with a delegation from the Standing Committee of the General Confederation of Labor (CGT) in the evening to discuss the situation of the labor unrest. CGT Secretary-General Stonehouse was also present. It was decided that the government and the CGT would jointly take various measures to ensure that the capital's food supply would not be depleted and that false information would not be spread. Stonehouse gave a radio address that evening, stating that the strike movement was purely occupational in nature, and that striking workers and trade unions must strive to maintain this and not allow it to be mixed with other purposes. Finally, he asked the government to quickly take all necessary measures to end the labor unrest. (Havas dispatch, 5th)

(Paris) After Prime Minister Léon Blum's broadcast speech on the resolution of the labor unrest, people's minds were greatly reassured, and it was generally believed that the strike movement could be ended and economic activity could be restored to its original state. The stock exchange has already felt the positive impact, and various securities have shown improvement. Government bonds rose by two francs, and Banque de France shares were quoted at 325 francs. Although foreign securities felt hesitant and uncertain at the opening, they uniformly rose shortly after. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

(Paris) Since the outbreak of the strike, it has been eleven days without incident. Until yesterday, employees of several discount department stores and shops announced a strike. Although employees of companies transporting newspapers continue to strike, newspapers have switched to using street vendors, and residents can still get a copy in hand without difficulty. Various public utilities, such as tap water, gas, and electricity, are still operating as usual, and there is no shortage of milk or other food. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

(Paris) The total number of striking workers in various industries in the capital area has increased to as many as 210,000 this morning. In the northern provinces, as of this evening, there are 90,000. Workers belonging to the vegetable market in the capital have signed a contract with their employers and are preparing to resume work. In addition, in the newspaper industry, managers of various newspapers belonging to the Popular Front held a meeting in the afternoon to study ways to publish their newspapers as usual. (Havas dispatch, 5th)

(Paris) The Paris City Council, fearing that the strike would affect the food supply of the people, convened an emergency meeting yesterday to discuss it. The Prefect of the Seine, Vile, issued a statement, stating, "There is no need to panic about the current situation. Various public utilities are currently operating as usual. The supply of electricity and gas is not experiencing difficulties. The subway and buses are also operating as usual," etc. Striking workers throughout the city are still avoiding violent actions or conflicts with employers. The police have also not come out to intervene. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

The labor unrest in Dunkirk and Douai, France, continues to expand, with a total of 20,000 striking workers. There is a risk of a general strike in the Aniche and Escarpelles coal mining areas, as well as the coking plants and electricity conversion stations. However, the electricity required by the city and its surrounding areas can still be supplied normally without interruption. In addition, labor unrest has also occurred in Provin, where the clay extraction workers have also gone on strike. Major stores in the city of Lille, including food stores and department stores, have closed. Workers at major breweries have occupied factory buildings. Of the 5,100 workers at the shipyards, 1,500 have gone on strike. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

(Paris) A private unlicensed radio station broadcast unfounded news this morning, stating that employees of one of the major banks in Paris, namely Crédit Lyonnais, had announced a strike. Finance Minister Auriol has asked Justice Minister Luca to investigate and prosecute. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Talk Lasts Half an Hour

(London) Foreign Secretary Eden drove to the residence of Shanghai tycoon Sir Victor Sassoon at 2:00 p.m. to visit the Emperor of Abyssinia. The conversation lasted only half an hour before he left. No statement was issued afterwards. Eden's trip was only a courtesy call and lasted a very short time, so the current situation of the Italo-Ethiopian issue would not have been discussed. It is rumored that the Ethiopian Emperor may go to Rome to negotiate with Italian Prime Minister Mussolini in person. This news has not been confirmed. Its source comes from one of the following four areas: Ethiopian Minister Dr. Martin is scheduled to host a banquet at the embassy tomorrow to welcome the Emperor, and has invited prominent British figures and members of the diplomatic corps to accompany him. Currently, aside from Chinese Ambassador Dr. Guo Taiqi, Turkish Ambassador Fethi, Japanese Chargé d'affaires Fujii, Iranian Minister Kamara, and British Liberal Party leader Lloyd George, who have agreed to participate, Foreign Secretary Eden has declined twice and will send Undersecretary Lord Cranborne to represent him at the banquet. Ambassadors from other countries, such as France, Russia, Brazil, and Chile, are currently not in London and will send representatives to attend the banquet, which makes the Ethiopian Emperor feel unhappy. Foreign Secretary Eden visited the Ethiopian Emperor today, and at the same time, Minister Martin also met with the head of the Abyssinian affairs section of the Foreign Office, Penderson (the Italo-Ethiopian dispute resolution plan proposed by former French Prime Minister Laval and former British Foreign Secretary Sir Samuel Hoare was drafted by Penderson and Saint-Quentin, assistant head of the African Affairs Division of the French Foreign Ministry). It is rumored that the Ethiopian Emperor is very dissatisfied with the results of the two men's conversation. It has been rumored that Italian Prime Minister Mussolini is very willing to contact the Ethiopian Emperor face-to-face, and the Ethiopian Emperor recently gave an interview to a reporter from the Daily Telegraph, saying that his purpose in coming to Europe was to make all conversations more convenient with him present, which is highly valued by the general public. French aviator, the Ethiopian Emperor's aviation advisor, Trouillat (who previously flew to Ethiopia privately, landed in Italy en route, was escorted back to France, and was subsequently released), suddenly came here from France today, so the general public speculates that Trouillat's purpose here is to fly the Emperor to another location. The above points are the sources of rumors from outside. However, according to a statement issued by the Ethiopian Embassy, the Emperor intends to go to Switzerland from here, but does not intend to go to Geneva. British officials are very satisfied with this news. In addition, a British women's organization called the "Peace Crusade" is scheduled to hold a meeting at "Queen's Hall" on the 15th of this month. At that time, the Ethiopian Emperor's daughter, Princess Tsehai, will attend and give a speech. It is said that Princess Tsehai's decision to come to England was at the invitation of that organization. (Havas dispatch, 5th)

(Geneva) The chairman of the League of Nations Council, British Foreign Secretary Eden, has suggested to the representatives of the member states of the Council that he intends to choose the 26th of this month as the date for the extraordinary meeting of the Council. This is acceptable to the representatives and will be officially decided before Tuesday next week. (Havas dispatch, 5th)

US Republican Party Convention Candidates for President Still in Competition 40

Cleveland: The National Republican Convention is scheduled to open here on the 9th of this month. Hundreds of party members have arrived here today. The Republican Party is preparing to vigorously attack President Roosevelt's New Deal with the slogan "Help So-and-so (the name of the Republican presidential candidate will be filled in after he is nominated) Restore Sanity." Many sources currently predict that Kansas Governor Landon has hope of being nominated as a presidential candidate. The convention has a total of 1,001 delegates, of whom about 800 are attending without instructions from any faction. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

US Senate Passes Tax Bill Totaling $829 Million 41

Washington: The Senate today passed an $829,000,000 tax bill by a vote of 38 to 24, to redistribute income tax paid by individuals and corporations. The bill stipulates that the following income taxes will be collected: 15 to 18 percent of corporate income, which the Treasury Department estimates will collect approximately $215,000,000; 7 percent of corporate surplus, which will yield $217,000,000; 4 percent of shareholder dividends, which will yield $90,000,000; 22 percent of foreign companies in the United States, which will yield $4,000,000; an increase in special taxes on incomes between $6,000 and $50,000, which will yield $50,000,000; 80 percent of the agricultural adjustment administration's handling tax, which will yield $82,000,000; and a levy on vegetable oils and fats, which will yield $1,000,000. In addition to the direct levies mentioned above, the bill also aims to amend current law to encourage corporate liquidation, which is estimated to yield an additional $63,000,000 compared to before; closing loopholes in corporate reserve funds, which can increase government tax revenue by $40,000,000; and amending the kerosene tax to increase government tax revenue by $10,000,000. (National Telegram, 5th)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance recently telegraphed the Jiangsu Provincial Government, stating, "The seizure of smuggled goods in Tongshan and Wujin counties is highly commendable. The captured smugglers have been ordered to be sent to the customs for processing. As for smugglers who are foreign nationals with consular jurisdiction, please order them to be sent to the nearest consulate for investigation and handling. If they are Chinese nationals or foreign nationals without consular jurisdiction, please order them to be sent to military or judicial organs for interrogation in accordance with the Provisional Regulations for Punishing Evasion of Customs Duties previously consulted. Please also inform your subordinates that all future smuggling cases should be handled in this way. (Central News Agency dispatch, 6th)

The Situation in Palestine Worsens Again; Arabs Expand Strike and Market Closure; Military Police Intervene; Civilian Casualties Continue 45

Jerusalem - The Arab Central Strike Committee has decided to expand the general strike movement, leading to a sense of hopelessness in Palestine greater than ever before. Although the authorities have promulgated new emergency regulations, the Arabs have other new plans, attempting to involve other important businesses in the strike. This move will have even more serious developments. The attitude of the strike leaders is extremely tough. The government insists that negotiations can only begin after the Arabs stop the strike and local security is restored. Their main demand concerns the immigration of Jews into Palestine. In the past few days, although there have only been minor, illegal riots, the situation has become increasingly serious because Palestine is now seen as a "key" by other Eastern countries, and they are all closely watching its developments. According to reliable sources, the people of Syria are also considering the attitude and strategy they should take if the current negotiations in Paris with France on the covenant unfortunately break down. (Reuters, 6th)

Economic Miscellany 56

— Edited by Tang Qingzeng

Emphasis on Agriculture? Emphasis on Industry (Part 2) - Zeng Diguang

Regarding the issue of economic transformation in China, some advocate emphasizing agriculture, some advocate emphasizing industry, and some advocate emphasizing both agriculture and industry. The arguments of each faction are summarized as follows:

Reasons for Advocating Emphasis on Agriculture: The profound agricultural panic and the intense poverty of farmers in recent years have led informed people to believe that the transformation of China's economy must begin with agriculture. In addition to actually participating in rural construction, they have put forward the following arguments to awaken the attention of the people:

(A) China has taken agriculture as the foundation of the country for thousands of years, so developing agriculture is to consolidate the foundation of the country;

(B) The number of people engaged in agriculture in China accounts for the largest majority of the population, so developing agriculture is to seek happiness for the largest majority of the people;

(C) The deepening of China's economic panic is due to the decline of the rural economy, so developing agriculture is a strategy to alleviate China's economic panic;

(D) Under its historical and international environment, China's economic development can only be based on agriculture;

(E) The rural economy is dependent on industry and commerce, so developing the countryside is to consolidate the foundation of industry and commerce;

(F) If the rural economy can be consolidated, rural order can be stabilized, and peasant unrest can be reduced;

(G) If the countryside can be revived, the surplus population in cities can be reduced;

(H) If the rural economy can prosper, financial problems can be easily solved.

Reasons for Advocating Emphasis on Industry: Those who advocate that the transformation of China's economy should emphasize industry believe that "the contribution of muscle-powered production methods to the welfare of the people is definitely not as great as that of mechanized production methods." Therefore, they advocate that the transformation of China's economy should take the road of industrialization. Their main arguments include the following six points:

(A) The economic foundation of all countries in the world is centered on the industrial economy. China's economy is a part of the world economy, so its economic development should also follow this track to avoid falling behind and becoming abnormal.

(B) European and American countries that take industry as the focus of the national economy are all able to become rich and strong. China is in a state of poverty and weakness because its industry is underdeveloped.

(C) The most serious crisis in China at present is caused by the continuous influx of industrial products from the great powers. Therefore, in order to save this crisis, we should quickly revitalize the national industry to resist it.

(D) If industry can develop, we can use all raw materials. As a result, the income of farmers can be increased, rural finance can be enriched, and the livelihood of farmers can be stabilized, thereby stabilizing the foundation of the entire national economy.

(E) It is not impossible to seek China's industrialization. If we can strive to improve production methods, factory management, and humbly adopt the strengths of others, the future will be bright.

(F) If the government and financiers can cooperate effectively with industrialists, there will be no problem in seeking the industrialization of China's economic construction.

On balance, although the reasons listed by the two factions above each have a piece of the truth, both have inappropriate aspects. Those who advocate that China's economic construction should be centered on agriculture deny the absolute necessity of China's economic industrialization due to their adherence to the traditional idea of agriculture as the foundation of the country, which is their most serious mistake. Second, modern economy is centered on industry. If we do not conform to the times and only seek to revive agriculture alone, it is an abnormal restoration movement, which cannot be allowed by the principles of economic development. Third, if agricultural construction is to proceed smoothly, the industrial economy must provide excellent technology, sophisticated machinery, abundant capital, and a large number of talents in order to achieve success. Fourth, even if separate agricultural construction can be realized, it cannot save China's current economic crisis, and it will only become a market monopolized by the great powers. The opinions of those who advocate that the transformation of China's economy should be centered on industry are also inevitably biased and do not pay attention to the following issues: Before the foundation of China's rural economy has been thoroughly changed, it is impossible to thoroughly industrialize China's economic construction; Under the oppression of political and economic violence of the great powers, it is very difficult to revitalize the national industry. The collapse of emerging national industries in recent years can serve as a warning; If China's economic construction is to be centered on industry, there must be sufficient funds to achieve success. China is already so poor, where will the funds come from? The inconvenience of transportation, the oppression of excessive taxes, and feudal exploitation, etc., if they are not quickly eliminated, it will not be easy for China's economic development to focus on industry; If China's economic construction is centered on industry, rural capital will at least temporarily become poor, and peasant unrest will become more dangerous.

It can be seen that the development of China's economy, if only focusing on one aspect, is definitely not the best strategy. Moreover, the current international environment is extremely bad, and we will inevitably encounter endless resistance. Only with the greatest perseverance and the final determination can we proceed on both sides. In rural areas, we should engage in rural transformation work, actively train the people, and strengthen their power, so that the vast peasant masses can unite with each other and develop China's economy. At the same time, in urban areas, we should engage in the construction of small-scale industries, so that the absolute necessities of life can gradually become self-sufficient. Therefore, the foundation of China's national economy should be built on agriculture, and the scope of the economy should be expanded by industry and commerce, complementing each other and not favoring one over the other.

Miscellaneous Writings on Rural Hubei (Special Correspondent of This Newspaper, Cheng) 61

(16) Trivial Talks on the Life of Farmers in Fang County and Zhushan

The reporter came from the north to investigate, with Jun County, Yun County, Fang County, and Zhushan as the destinations, intending to first take a car to Jun County, then transfer to a mountain sedan chair to Yunyang, and then turn to Fang County and Zhushan. Unexpectedly, when he arrived at Shihua Street, which belongs to Gucheng County, the car was anxiously heading north, as if waiting for the car to arrive in Jun County, I don't know when. When I asked at the station, there was no definite answer. They only said that the bridge at a certain place had not been repaired yet. However, if the bridge is repaired, it will take five or six sunny days after the rain to dry the road before traffic can pass. If the weather changes during the road drying period, you have to wait again. The trip to Jun County and Yun County had to be abandoned because of this. As for Fang County, Zhushan and other counties, the roads are dark and winding, and it is impossible to reach them in more than a month. Moreover, ambushes occur from time to time, and there is no guarantee at all, which is also impossible. I had to turn back halfway. Mo Di turned his car around, which was very different from his original intention. However, when I was in Shihua Street, I heard a lot about the living conditions of farmers in Fang County and Zhushan. I would like to record it as follows:

The so-called Fang County and Zhushan refer to Fang County, Zhushan County, and Zhuxi County. The three counties are listed side by side, Fang County is on the left and right, Zhushan is in the middle, and Zhuxi is on the left. They are all mountain countries and belong to the Eighth Administrative Region of Yunyang. Fang County was formerly known as Fangling. Emperor Zhongzong of the Tang Dynasty was deposed and built a city to live here. The territory is second only to Sui County in terms of area, and the length is even more distant. Because it is surrounded by mountains, as solid as a house, it is named the county. It is commonly known as "Fang County at the bottom of ten thousand mountains." It is also eight or nine hundred miles long, but not as wide, so there is a saying that "Fang County is a thousand miles long like a line." Zhushan and Zhuxi were ancient Yong countries, and were divided into two counties until the Ming Dynasty. They are purely agricultural societies. Paddy fields in Fang Prefecture account for one-tenth or two-tenths, and mountains account for eight-tenths or nine-tenths. Calculated in terms of stone, the standard of stone is determined by the amount of planting. The main agricultural products are wheat, beans, and corn. The by-products are black and white fungus, tung oil, raw lacquer, fire paper, gallnuts, medicinal materials, and black fungus, with an annual output of more than 100,000 catties, worth 200,000 yuan. 10,000 baskets of tung oil are worth 100,000 yuan. Paddy fields in Zhushan account for two-tenths, and dry land and barren mountains account for eight-tenths. Corn, wheat, and miscellaneous grains are the main crops, and tung oil and fungus are also abundant as by-products. Cultivated land is calculated in stone, and there is no term for mu. Paddy fields in Zhuxi account for one-third, and mountains account for two-thirds. The products are rice, wheat, potatoes, corn, beans, cotton, and land is also calculated in stone. One stone per tree, converted to one mu of field. Farmers rely on the weather to make a living. There is no convenience for ponds to irrigate. Paddy fields rely entirely on ditch water, harbor water, and rapids. Simple weirs and dams are built to guide irrigation. When the water is cut off, the rice will wither. Mountain land depends more on rainwater. In dry years, there is no relief. However, once it rains, the ridges under the mountains will be flooded, and the sand from the mountains will pour down. In addition to the ridges being crushed, the rivers will also be silted up. In the past, opium was mostly grown in the mountains, but now it has completely disappeared. These places where opium was grown are areas where inspection and eradication committee members or local officials cannot easily reach. The people stopped growing opium voluntarily, not because they were afraid of strict laws, but because the local gentry were inferior and exploited too much, making it not worth the loss. It is also a fortunate thing that the poisonous weeds can be completely eradicated. The mountains are extremely rich in minerals, with all kinds of metals, and especially abundant coal, which is readily available. It is a pity that it has not been mined. Although copper mines were once manually mined, they were soon discontinued. Zhushan has a special mine, which is rich in green stone, which is sold to foreign countries and abroad. Westerners use it to make toys, and lamas use it to make rosary beads, which are very precious. There are many kinds of animals, such as tigers, leopards, wild boars, deer, chickens, deer, and rabbits. Monkeys are especially abundant in the mountains.

Because the counties are covered with mountains and forests are deep, transportation is extremely inconvenient. There are few pedestrians on the road, and they must bring dry food and salt when traveling. Therefore, there are those who grow old and die without contacting each other. The difficulty of the road is described in a proverb: "Lice go backwards, ghosts are worried, and the King of Hell shakes his head three times when he sees it." The bird path in the Silkworm Mountain is hardly enough to compare with this. Farmers in the mountains mostly live alone, and their houses are very simple. Some live in caves, do not light lamps at night, and live with wild animals. In Fang County, one Bao chief covers dozens of miles, and one Lian Bao chief covers four hundred miles. It is extremely difficult to implement government orders. For example, if you summon strong men for training, you can only gather more than ten people in a few days. Villages with dozens of households must be of the same surname and clan. The clan chief must be a bully, like the native officials of ancient times. Those who own guns are like chieftains. Therefore, the district chiefs appointed by the government are all "sitting tigers" of this kind. The government must also listen to their orders. These district chiefs are all sitting tigers, fearing to fall on the plains, and are unwilling to enter the city. They have the concept of "listening to the call but not listening to the announcement." They receive the county government's orders while sitting, which is considered polite. Whether to comply or not is not what they pay attention to, nor is it what the government dares to ask. Generally, matters relating to the county government are handled by representatives from the city office. For example, Zhu Fengzhang, the district chief of Zhushan, is one of them. Now that he has committed a serious crime, the gunmen have been dismissed and he will be purged. Others are still too numerous to remove.

The rural economy is absolutely bankrupt. The food produced is not enough to eat. The by-products such as raw lacquer, tung oil, fungus, and medicinal materials cannot be transported out due to inconvenient transportation. A few farmers do not avoid hardship and carry goods out of the mountains on their shoulders, but it is difficult to transport much. The common currency among the people is still silver dollars. Although legal tender has been introduced, they cannot distinguish between genuine and fake, and they rarely use it. Even in cities, it is impossible to exchange five-yuan legal tender. Therefore, farmers who transport goods out of the mountains must obtain silver dollars to return to the mountains. At this time, when legal tender is being promoted, merchants from other counties deliberately exploit them. They lose 20% or 30% when exchanging goods worth 100 yuan for silver dollars. Now they have changed to trading goods. Foreign goods can be imported continuously, and Japanese goods are especially popular because of their low prices. In remote areas, the economic power of foreigners has penetrated unimpeded, which is worrying.

The life of farmers is extremely difficult. In the past, they had "no half a liter of rice a day and no half a bed at night." In recent years, there have been successive droughts and floods, coupled with the frequent intrusions of Red bandits, bandits, routed soldiers, Yu bandits, Shaanxi bandits, and Sichuan bandits, as well as the long-term demands of native officials and chieftains. Their flesh and blood are exhausted, and their vitality has been cut off. Most farmers do not know what rice is or what salt tastes like. Yesterday in Gucheng, I personally saw telegrams from the garrison in Fang County and Zhushan and from legal groups, saying that tree bark and grass roots have been eaten up. It is probably not a false statement. Also, because very little cotton is produced, some people have never worn cotton clothes in their lives. This kind of life is suspected to be inhuman. The climate in the mountains is unpredictable. It snows in August and does not melt until March of the following year. At the same time, one mountain has four kinds of climates. The top layer is sunny, the second layer has clouds and mist, the third layer snows, and the fourth layer rains. Due to the climate, people roast fire in all seasons and are prone to diseases. The strangest disease is "goiter," which is caused by a certain toxin in the leaves on the trees that fall into the water. When people drink it, they get this disease. At first, there is only a scar under the neck, which gradually grows bigger, even as big as a five-stone gourd, hanging down to the chest. Those who are pierced through the head die. Eight out of ten people suffer from this disease, and they are not surprised because they are used to it. On the contrary, if people from other counties enter the area and see no "goiter," they feel strange. Those who smoke opium do not suffer from this disease. Eating more kelp and applying iodine will also prevent it. Those who are ill can also be cured. The former is the truth, and the latter was invented by people from other counties. However, the locals are very poor, and kelp and iodine are not cheap. Although they know the method, they have no ability to cure it. There is also the disease of rotten eyes. About five or six out of ten people suffer from it, probably because it is contagious due to uncleanliness.

The wheel of time is stagnant in the Middle Ages. The low level of education is also a major reason. The degree of lowness is laughable when heard. Although primary schools are maintained in the county seat, the equipment is simple, teachers are lacking, and there are no new textbooks. The principal of a certain school in Zhushan calls himself a "foreign teacher." Most of the students are over 24 or 5 years old, and some are over 30. Their purpose in studying is not to have the lofty ambition of promoting morality and benefiting the people, nor to have the ambition of being promoted to officialdom, becoming rich, and ennobling their wives and children. They are specially learning to write complaints in order to prepare for lawsuits with others. Therefore, official documents and lawyer drafts are widely collected into books and recited fluently. The land is neither known nor urgent to them. As for rural primary schools, it can be said that there are none at all. Even private schools are few. The number of illiterates accounts for more than 96%. They cannot recognize official documents and announcements.

In summary, in both spirit and matter, the situation of farmers in Fang County and Zhushan is different from that of human beings in the world. The first step in relief is to open up roads and develop transportation, so that culture can be imported and goods can be exported. From here to Fang County, the 82nd Division's engineering unit has repaired the roadbed. Only two mountains have not yet been blasted. If the government and the people continue to build it, it will be completed in time. However, it is difficult to design between the two Zhus. (Sent from Shihua Street on May 18)

Complete Qin Tile Volume Discovered in Zou County, Shandong Province. Many Ocher Pottery Shards Discovered. Han Stone Carvings Also Abundant in Yi County 62

Jinan correspondence, Zou County is the hometown of Confucius and Mencius, and occupies an important position in the history of women's transformation. The ancient city of Zhu Kingdom is located in the county, along with Teng County and Yi County nearby, all of which were the ancient states of Teng and Xue in the Spring and Autumn Period. In recent years, antiquities have been discovered, mostly from the Qin and Han Dynasties, which are valued by archaeologists. The Han stone carvings and other items currently on display in the Shandong Provincial Library were mostly transported from the Zou and Teng areas and are treasured by the world. Wang Xiantang, the director of the library, recently traveled to Zou County to collect antiquities to help study ancient culture. He returned to Jinan yesterday. According to the results of the Zou trip, a brief record is as follows:

Qin Dynasty Tile Volume Zou County is also known as Ji Wangcheng, which is the capital of the ancient Zhu Kingdom. The remains of the rammed-earth city wall are still intact. Many pottery shards with inscriptions are produced in the city. The most valuable is the Qin Dynasty tile volume, which has an edict of Emperor Qin Shi Huang in the twenty-sixth year, which was printed with ten seals. The calligraphy is ancient. Chen , a famous antique connoisseur and collector from Weixian County in the Qing Dynasty, studied the text on the tile volume and determined that it was written by Li Si with a brush. Therefore, Chen once commented that "the legacy of the prime minister Li Si, the ancestor of soft brushes." According to Qin volumes, weights, and measures, the earliest one seen in the inscription is Yan's Family Instructions from the Sui Dynasty. Later, they were discovered in the Song, Ming, and Qing Dynasties. Archaeologists have also recorded many of them, but they are all made of iron or copper. Later, Chen discovered tile volume pottery shards. After 30 years of searching, he was able to piece together dozens of pottery shards into a complete vessel, which he considered an unprecedented discovery and a rare treasure. Because tile volume shards are only produced in Zou County, it took 30 years to piece together a complete vessel, which is really not easy. Unfortunately, after Chen's death, the volume was purchased by the Japanese. Now, a complete tile volume has been discovered in Zou County, which is intact and has been acquired by the Provincial Library.

Ocher Pottery Shards Pottery shards with ocher and patterns were previously discovered by archaeologists in the ancient city of Yan (northern Jiangsu), which was unique to other places. Therefore, it was considered a unique cultural product of "Yan" city and was greatly valued. Recently, many have also been discovered in Zou County, and they are exactly the same as those discovered in "Yan" city, which can prove that the State of Zhu in the Spring and Autumn Period also produced this object, which is the same as the culture of the State of Yan. The argument that ocher pottery shards are a unique culture of the State of Yan has added a material for archaeologists.

Anyang Han Stele Yi County has Anyang City, which was the capital of Marquis Anyang in the Former Han Dynasty. The locals still call it An Wangcheng. In fact, the marquis was not a king. There is a tomb mountain with seventy or eighty ancient tombs, which are lined up one after another, and the scale is several times larger than the Cao Wang Tomb in Teng County. The tomb pits are all Han Dynasty stone carvings with excellent patterns. The farmers' wall foundations in nearby villages are mostly made of Han stone carvings, which are readily available. The locals do not cherish them very much. However, because there are too many, it is impossible to transport them to Jinan for preservation.

Educational Broadcasting Special Issue

One of the Biology Lectures: The Contribution of Biology to Mankind (Part 1) 63

— Xue Deyu, Director of the Natural Science Group of the Zhengzhong Book Company Translation Office

In the natural world surrounding us, there are two kinds of things: one is inanimate and the other is animate. The study of the various phenomena of inanimate things is called physical science; the study of the various phenomena of animate things is called biology. Biology did not begin today. More than two thousand years ago, during the most brilliant period of Greek civilization, there was a scholar named Aristotle who began to study various phenomena in biology. However, from Aristotle until the fifteenth century, there was no significant progress or development, because the power of Christianity was too strong at that time, and religion continued to oppress science, causing facts and superstitions to be mixed up. Modern biology took shape in the early nineteenth century, only two hundred years ago. The progress in these two hundred years is like the rising sun in the east. To mention the most prominent ones: the first is the establishment of the cell theory; the second is the proof of biological evolution. These two points are explained separately below:

More than two hundred years ago, the British botanist Robert Hoore cut a thin layer of cork and observed it under a very simple microscope. He discovered that the cork was made up of many honeycomb-like groups, which he called cells. After further research by many scholars, it was also known that the honeycomb-like cells were not empty, but filled with extremely complex substances. In the nineteenth century, the German zoologist Schwann discovered that the animal body was also made up of very small cells. At the same time, the German botanist Schleiden discovered that plant cells and animal cells were generally the same. Thanks to the research of these two scholars, it was only then that animals and plants, which were previously considered unrelated, were fundamentally determined to be passed down from the same ancestor. The mingling of the animal and plant kingdoms has indeed made great progress in human intelligence, and it has also given us the hint that "there is another world under the microscope."

The cell is to the organism as the unit of weight is the gram and the unit of length is the centimeter, and it can be said to be the unit of the organism. Moreover, the cell is not only the source of life phenomena in the organism, but also the heredity phenomenon that children resemble their parents is a function of the cell. Therefore, the focus of research in physiology, genetics, and other branches of biology is concentrated on cells. In other words, the foundation of biology should be built on cells. If the principle of cells is not understood, the function of the living body cannot be understood. Furthermore, if the question of life is not thoroughly studied at the cellular level, it will never be resolved.

The organism is made up of cells, but how are the cells that produce life born? This kind of thought lingers in our minds. Originally, human beings are very smart. All questions that human intelligence cannot explain are often entrusted to heaven and to God in order to shirk his own responsibility. Regarding the life of organisms in the past thousands of years, it was also once entrusted to God. After the progress of cytology, it was only then that we knew that the life of cells cannot be created out of nothing. Only cells can produce cells. In other words, without existing life, it is impossible to discover objects with continued life.

Before the discovery of cells, several scholars knew that there were microorganisms invisible to the naked eye in nature—protozoa or bacteria. More than two hundred and fifty years ago, the Dutchman Leeuwenhoock studied various objects with a toy-like microscope. One day, he took a drop of rainwater and observed it under a microscope. He discovered that countless extremely active minute animals and plants were lurking in the rainwater. He reported this to the academic community, but few people responded. Fortunately, Mr. Lei was wealthy and still worked tirelessly in his research. He finally discovered a method of movement of certain bacteria and protozoa as well as blood cells in the human body. Thus, the world began to know of the existence of microorganisms. At that time, scholars were already deeply convinced that fish were oviparous and beasts were viviparous, which was tantamount to admitting that organisms could only produce organisms. However, after the discovery of microorganisms, witnessing the rapid reproduction of many small organisms in a short period of time, the idea that these small organisms were suddenly generated—created by God—was revived. Although there were one or two outstanding scholars who resolutely opposed it, they had not grasped any solid evidence until the cell theory was established. Afterwards, the structure of the microscope improved, and microorganisms became more and more developed. It was only then that it became clear that microorganisms composed of single cells could not be discovered without seeds. The theory of creation by God was thus self-defeating.

To discuss how life came about and how organisms came about seems to be the idea of the leisure class and has little to do with life, but biology is one of the great contributions to human history, so I would like to specifically discuss the relationship between cell theory and microorganisms:

Leeuwenhoek discovered microorganisms, and then it became clear that microorganisms are also produced by cells. Does this have nothing to do with life? Thirty or forty years ago, the French brewing industry experienced a great panic that almost bankrupted it. That is, the wines and other alcoholic beverages that the French relied on for their lives were all corrupted and could not be recovered. At that time, the famous French chemist Pastenr investigated the cause of the corruption and discovered that the fermentation of well-known wines, wines, and other alcoholic beverages, which was previously unknown, was the action of a type of microorganism called fermenting bacteria. Because of the fermentation of these bacteria, the raw materials for winemaking can be turned into wine. At the same time, he also discovered that there is often an abnormal fermentation phenomenon during brewing, that is, the fermentation is mixed with microorganisms that corrupt the wine, then the finished wine will be corrupt and unsuitable for drinking. Not only is wine like this, but also when the human body or other organic bodies decay, it is nothing more than the action of bacteria. After discovering this phenomenon, Mr. Ba continued to study it and thought that all the diseases of livestock and humans might also be caused by these microorganisms. After countless experiments, he finally understood the relationship between diseases and microorganisms. At that time, the silkworm industry in France also faced a huge problem, that is, silkworms developed a most terrible disease—microparticle disease, which almost caused the silkworm industry in France to collapse. Mr. Ba devoted himself to research and finally discovered that the disease of silkworms was also caused by a type of bacteria. Therefore, he took measures to prevent it and was finally able to save the desperate situation. Later, Mr. Ba also determined the pathogens of tetanus and rabies and heard of the way to treat such diseases by injecting serum. Now we can prevent various infectious diseases in advance and save them afterwards, which can be said to be directly related to the study of Mr. Ba.

All Jiangxi Business Federation Conference. 80 Representatives Attended. All Hope to Relieve the Market 64

Sixty-two chambers of commerce out of 119 chambers of commerce in the province, with 80 representatives, and more than 100 guests, including representatives from party and government agencies, as well as executive and supervisory committee members from provincial and municipal chambers of commerce, attended. Record of the Rupture of the Zhongxiang Xiang Embankment: Zhongxiang, Tianmen, and Hanchuan Counties Entirely Submerged; Embankment Workers All Escaped, Only the Villagers Suffered 65

E Province:

Regarding the ten counties and cities of Zhongxiang, Jingmen, Tianmen, Qianjiang, etc., the sole guarantee of taxation; since the rupture last autumn, the National Economic Council and the Hubei Provincial Government have actively planned repairs. Due to the difficulty of constructing the breach at the third and fourth work sections, a remote embankment was rebuilt, stretching from Jiukou to Luohan Temple, a distance of eighteen and a half kilometers. In addition, a water interception dam and a cutoff dam were built at Xiongjiaqiao, requiring an expenditure of more than 2.7 million yuan, and mobilizing over 100,000 laborers. The scale of the project was unprecedented in the nation. Unexpectedly, after several months of construction, just as it was about to be completed, it was suddenly breached by the Han River on the night of May 26, and the effort was ruined. It is most regrettable. Zhongxiang, Tianmen, and Hanchuan counties have once again suffered disaster. One day after the embankment rupture, the reporter rushed to the work site to inspect the entire embankment and hereby records the situation as follows:

The remote embankment was divided into four work sections, with laborers conscripted from the five counties of Jingmen, Tianmen, Qianjiang, and Hanchuan for construction. The project was considered relatively solid. The fourth section was contracted and constructed by the Zhongxiang Xiang Embankment Engineering Office of the Economic Council. Due to the later start of construction and the difficulty in obtaining materials and the substandard work, cracks appeared even before completion. Although the personnel on the embankment knew the danger of this section, they still hoped that the water level would stabilize and that it could be completed after a considerable period. Unexpectedly, on the 25th, the water level in Yunyang suddenly rose by seven or eight meters, and in Xiangyang, it rose by one zhang (about 3.3 meters). As the warning came, the entire embankment was shaken. At 10:00 AM on the 26th, the head of the water reached the outside of the water interception dam. The momentum was not very strong at first. If timely rescue measures were taken, there was still hope of recovery. However, Xi Dejiong, the Director of the Jianghan Engineering Bureau and concurrently the Director of the embankment Engineering Office, and Shi Yuling, the Special Commissioner of the Third Administrative District and concurrently the Deputy Director of the Engineering Office, were away on official business in Jinghan. Without important personnel in charge, prompt action could not be taken. On the side of the Coordination and Repair Committee, County Magistrate Yu of Qianjiang, County Magistrate Zhou of Tianmen, and County Magistrate Gao of Hanchuan were stationed at sections one, two, and three, respectively, supervising the work. Only County Magistrate Xiong of Zhongxiang, County Magistrate Zhu of Jingmen, and Technician Chen Zhang of the Construction Department were stationed at the General Engineering Office. They urgently consulted with Chief Technician Feng, mainly to concentrate the laborers to complete the embankment section of less than forty-six meters and again requested the Engineering Office to prepare more materials and construction funds for use. They also notified the county magistrates stationed in each section to intensify supervision and speed up construction. Chief Engineer Lin Youlong and Deputy Engineer Liu of the Engineering Office went to Jiukou to excavate the lock mouth. The head of the Works Section was responsible for the rescue work at the fourth section. At 8:00 PM, the water level continued to rise. At the Xiongjiaqiao benchmark, reaching 44.6 meters, several breaches appeared in the cutoff dam. At 8:30 PM, it collapsed. The villages within the dam, spanning dozens of miles, were completely submerged. At 10:30 PM, it stretched to the foot of the fourth section embankment. At 11:00 PM, the telephone lines were cut, indicating that it had collapsed following the water interception dam. It was late at night, and the engineering personnel had no way to provide relief. Some of the soldiers stationed on the embankment also withdrew their defenses. Tens of thousands of laborers, sacrificing themselves for embankment repair, and unripe wheat unharvested, new seedlings unsown. Once they saw the embankment collapse, they fled in panic. Tools and clothing were discarded all over the embankment, and the sound of crying shook the earth, causing extraordinary chaos. Except for the county magistrates controlling and stopping a portion of the laborers from fleeing, most of them immediately scattered. The breach of the remote embankment occurred at the fifty-sixth sub-section of the fourth section. Initially, it breached three hundred meters, and by 1:00 AM on the 27th, it had expanded to six hundred meters. The fifty-fifth and fifty-seventh sub-sections were also affected. The rapid torrent poured down like a collapsing mountain. Zhongxiang, Tianmen, and Hanchuan counties were largely submerged. When the reporter inspected the breach, he saw a vast expanse of water inside and outside the embankment. Many refugees climbed onto roofs and trees, crying out for help, a scene too terrible to bear. There were more than ten worker sheds in the path of the breach. It is said that only the laborers from three sheds escaped, and the rest were swept into the flood, with dozens of deaths. Not only was labor wasted, but also lives were lost. However, the engineering personnel of Fenglu, before the breach, took their families and luggage and fled, so no one suffered. Although they were very slow in handling affairs, they were extraordinarily quick to escape.

After the Collapse of the Remote Embankment, Rushing to Repair Other Dangerous Embankment Sections

Shi Yuling, the Deputy Director of the Engineering Office, rushed to the work site on the morning of the 29th. Hearing that many refugees in Zhongxiang had not escaped and had been without food for two days, facing imminent death, he immediately ordered boats to be used for rescue and allocated rice for distribution. That evening, Provincial Government Committee Member Fan Xixu and Jianghan Engineering Bureau Director Xi Dejiong also arrived from Hankou. Fan and Shi met and wept in each other's arms. Shi and the five county magistrates telegraphed the provincial government, stating that they, as personnel involved, were inescapably responsible and requested severe punishment. The sorrow and indignation were overflowing from the words. The telegram read, "To Chairman Yang Jun of the Wuchang Provincial Government: The fourth section of the Zhongxiang Xiang Embankment Engineering Office's own project collapsed last night, as reported by the county magistrates. Now we respectfully present the details to you. The original height of the cutoff and water interception dams at Xiongjiaqiao was set at 45 meters. Previously, Director Liu (Shoupeng), Committee Member Fan (Xixu), and the undersigned, fearing that the set height would be difficult to withstand the summer floods in May, instructed the office to borrow sacks in advance to build a one-meter sub-dam. On the evening of that day, the water level at that location was 44.6 meters, as verifiable in the office's water level report. Yet the dam failed at that time. The fourth section originally had a drainage ditch, which Committee Member Fan ordered to be blocked up long ago. This time, Xiangyang had telegraphed many times in advance about the flood, but that ditch only began to be blocked up at 8:00 PM that night. Just as construction began, the water arrived, rushing straight down and causing severe flooding in the downstream counties. Most of the able-bodied men in the counties were on the embankment, and the ripe wheat could not be harvested. This year's autumn harvest will also be hopeless. This embankment project mobilized counties for half a year, using hundreds of thousands of laborers and spending millions of yuan. The tangible and intangible losses to the people are even more incalculable. On that evening, most of the office staff evaded responsibility, and were in a state of panic. It is difficult to describe. Although the undersigned did not construct the dams and the fourth section, we are all personnel involved and are indeed inescapably responsible. We should be severely punished to apologize to the people and uphold national law. In urgent telegrams, we are at a loss for words. Shi Yuling, Deng Bing, Zhou Yuwen, Xiong Daochen, Zhu Yiyuan, Gao Zhichao, bow and report."

Fan Xiji also telegraphed the National Economic Council and the provincial government, advocating for blocking the breach. The telegram read, "I, Ji, arrived in Shagang at 6:00 PM today. I learned that the breach in the fourth section is about 500 meters and has already stabilized, with no further expansion. I plan to go to the location tomorrow morning with the engineering personnel to survey the breach and the water interception dam. Although the time is pressing and farming is busy, the remote embankment is too important. It is insufficient to continue blocking and building to answer the government above and the people below. Looking at the water level of the Xiang River over the years, there is no absolute certainty of a large rise during the summer flood. It is only necessary to provide sufficient price, explain the advantages and disadvantages, and there will be no shortage of laborers willing to enlist. My humble opinion is to block the water interception dam and the breach in the fourth section simultaneously. If one of the two can be accomplished, it will be helpful to the entire embankment. If this year's water level is not high, we may be able to complete it by luck. I know that it involves taking risks and costs a lot, but for the future of the country and the lives and property of the people within the embankment, it seems we have no choice but to do so. If it fails, we can only follow it to our deaths to apologize to the government and the people. As for the details of the breach and the construction plan, I will discuss it with the engineering personnel after the survey and then report in detail. Fan Xiji bows and reports." (Sent from Shagang on May 29)

The "Life and Death Society" in Xianyou, Fujian: An Illegal Civil Organization; Villagers Are Greatly Feared of It 66

Xiamen Dispatch: Fengting in the Second District of Xianyou County is known for its fierce folk customs and frequent illegal organizations. The Xinghua Black and White Flags originated here, and other groups such as the Ten-Sound Society, Yixing Society, and Three-Point Society are also very popular. Recently, the "Life and Death Society" has emerged in the Houlan Village area of Xinnan Township in the same district. The leader of the society is a Mr. Wang from Houlan Village, who calls himself the "General Manager." He directly controls over forty core members, who are called "Teachers." Each Teacher is in charge of a "Route" and can recruit an unlimited number of ordinary members. Each Teacher commands the ordinary members they recruited in their Route. The society's creed is "Loyalty, Courage, Righteousness, and Chivalry," and they have the oath, "We do not seek to be born on the same day of the same month, but we wish to die on the same day of the same month." Hence the name "Life and Death Society." The society worships Zhao Xuantan. To join, one must be introduced by two members and register with a Teacher. The Teacher sets a date to introduce the recruit to the General Manager, who then orders them to swear an oath before the Zhao Xuantan shrine, vowing to obey commands. During the oath, the new member is led by their Teacher and stands on the steps. Red candles are burned high in the hall, and two broadswords are hung crossed and inverted in the middle of the doorway. The new member ascends the steps, bows, and enters from under the swords. Standing on both sides, from the Xuan Tan down to the door with hanging swords, are the Teachers of each Route and important members, each holding weapons such as broadswords, spears, and handguns, pretending to strike the new member. The General Manager stands beside the incense table of the shrine. The new members, one by one, reach the altar, swear an oath before the deity, write their names, ages, and dates of birth on yellow paper, and burn it. The ashes are mixed with wine, and each person pricks their middle finger, sprinkles blood into the wine, and drinks a mouthful. The General Manager then, on behalf of all members of the society, bestows the society's secret code and symbol. Thus, they become a formal member. Upon joining, they must donate a certain amount to the fund based on their ability, at least two yuan. When members have conflicts with others, they resort to force. If money is needed, it is drawn from the fund. When the fund is exhausted, the Teachers of each Route are responsible for sharing the burden. Therefore, ordinary people fear the members of the Life and Death Society. Recently, He Aigu of Changba Village had a piece of land bordering a certain village in Houlan. A dispute arose, and He was almost beaten to death by members of the Life and Death Society. There have been many similar cases, all committed by the Life and Death Society. Therefore, people in the Fengting area of Xianyou are pale with fear. (June 4)

The Turmoil of Cigarette Unified Tax in Tianjin: The Hebei-Chahar Council Orders Local Payment; Chinese and Foreign Tobacco Merchants Unanimously Resist 67

Tianjin Dispatch: The cigarette merchants of Tianjin received an official letter from the Unified Tax Management Office of the Hebei, Chahar, Suiyuan, and Tianjin districts on the 2nd of this month, stating in brief: "All cigarette factories and companies in the provinces and cities of Hebei, Chahar, Pingjin, etc., regarding the matter of affixing stamps and paying taxes, should be allowed to directly handle it with the local Unified Tax Bureau. Since the Yizhong Company (i.e., the British American Tobacco Company) has a factory in Tianjin, it should be treated the same. Hereafter, all cigarettes sold and transported within the territory of Hebei, Chahar, Pingjin, whether imported or domestically produced, should be handled according to the following methods. The tax collection of the Yizhong Tobacco Company will temporarily be handled by the issuance of inspection certificates by this Council, stamped with a seal. All cigarette shipments from the company will be based on the affixing of inspection certificates and taxed according to grade. Cigarette shipments that have already been stamped and left the factory but have not been unpacked should be checked for certificates and supplementary taxes should be paid. Cigarette shipments imported from outside this territory should be stamped and supplementary taxes should be paid. Cigarette shipments transported to non-unified tax areas have always had a tax refund method, which will continue to be implemented." After this official letter was delivered to various tobacco firms and companies, all the tobacco merchants were greatly shocked. They believe that except for Yizhong and Zhenchang, which have factories manufacturing locally in Tianjin, the factories of other tobacco merchants are all located in Shanghai. The taxes have always been supervised and paid directly by the resident factory staff, and the stamps were affixed according to grade before they were allowed to be transported and sold. After arriving in Tianjin, the Tianjin Unified Tax Management Office only sent personnel to stamp a mark when the boxes were unpacked and sold, without collecting additional taxes. Now, in Hebei-Chahar territory, the inspection certificate procedure is implemented. Although the name is different, it is actually equivalent to double taxation. One item is taxed twice, which breaks the unified tax rule and increases the burden on tobacco merchants. This matter is close to extortion and is difficult to accept. On the morning of the 3rd, an emergency meeting was held at the Cigarette Merchants Association. Except for the Yizhong Company, which had other reasons and negotiated separately, a total of thirty-two companies, including Nanyang, Zhenzhong, Huamei, Huacheng, Yongyuan, Nanbeiyang, etc., attended. Wang Wendian, the chairman of the association, explained the orders of the Hebei-Chahar authorities and opened the discussion. Everyone agreed to oppose the double taxation in Hebei-Chahar territory. A telegram was sent to the Tax Department of the Ministry of Finance, the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee, and the Unified Tax Bureau of the Four Provinces of Hebei, Shanxi, Chahar, and Suiyuan, requesting that the order be withdrawn to maintain the tobacco merchants' livelihood. A telegram was also sent to Mayor Xiao of Peiping, praying that he would mediate with the Political Affairs Committee and relay to the Unified Tax Bureau of the Four Provinces to allow the sale of existing goods as soon as possible to maintain the market. Representatives were elected to petition the Pingjin authorities. On the night of the 4th, representatives from the Unified Tax Bureau of the Four Provinces notified the tobacco merchants that the second resolution of the association, allowing the sale of existing goods to maintain the market, was acceptable. However, before the tax issue is resolved, a guarantor should be found. If taxes still need to be paid in the future, the tobacco merchants should pay taxes according to regulations, and the guarantor will be responsible for those who are dishonest. The tobacco merchants felt that this measure was too harsh and expressed their inability to comply. Wang Wendian called Xiao Zhenying's residence in Peiping at midnight, requesting that Xiao uphold justice. However, Xiao was not at home. On the 5th, the Hebei-Chahar authorities did not respond to the tobacco merchants' appeals. As for the telegrams sent by the tobacco merchants to the Ministry of Finance, the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee, etc., they generally stated, "The domestic industry is already extremely depressed. If taxes are levied again, not only will the merchants be unable to bear the burden, but foreign merchants will be given the opportunity to sell their products. Please withdraw the order or handle it separately. Those with manufacturing plants in Tianjin should pay taxes in Tianjin. Those without manufacturing plants in Tianjin but manufactured in Shanghai, Qingdao, etc., and already affixed stamps before being transported to Tianjin should be exempt from supplementary taxes." On the morning of the 5th, the tobacco merchants gathered again and resolved four items: First, request the Unified Tax Bureau to allow personnel to stamp all goods taxed before June 2nd and allow them to be unpacked and sold. Second, if there is no satisfactory result in the near future, the merchants will automatically unpack the goods for the sake of maintaining business, stamp them with the seal of the association, and report them to the Unified Tax Bureau of the Four Provinces for emergency needs. Third, when necessary, they will still petition to achieve the purpose of canceling double taxation. According to the Cigarette Merchants Association, the total number of cigarettes sold in Tianjin and re-exported is about 1,600 boxes per month (each box averages 50,000 cigarettes). Currently, there are only 600 boxes remaining in the city. If this issue is delayed and unresolved, Chinese cigarettes will not be transported north, and foreign cigarettes will likely seize the opportunity to replace the market. Therefore, the general cigarette merchants are very anxious. Furthermore, since this matter occurred, the prices of various cigarettes have increased since the 5th. Those originally sold for 3.2 yuan per box have increased to 3.8 yuan, and those originally sold for 3.8 yuan have increased to 4.6 yuan. There is some panic about shortages in the market. However, those familiar with the unified tax and the situation of tobacco merchants speculate that the tobacco merchants will inevitably fail and submit to the tax payment. The only remedy is to take it from the smokers and increase the prices of all cigarettes uniformly. The situation on the 5th already shows the beginning of this trend, and it will inevitably become the trend in the future. However, sales will be affected by the price increase, which is expected. The Unified Tax Bureau is currently using a blockade method. If tobacco merchants do not pay taxes, personnel will be stationed at the factory, and they will not be allowed to transport and sell. Since it is located in the concession, it seems there is no way. However, if the previous strategy is adopted outside the concession, the arrival of tobacco merchants' goods will gradually be cut off, and they will still fail.

As for the British Yizhong Company, its general factory is located in Shanghai, and there is a branch factory in the Third Special District of Tianjin, with more than 2,000 male and female workers. The unified tax has always been paid directly according to a contract with the Ministry of Finance, without going through any unified tax bureau for collection. The two factories in Shanghai and Tianjin pay a total of one million yuan per month. Because it is paid at the beginning of each month, the Ministry of Finance actually receives only 750,000 yuan as a reward, with 250,000 yuan as a rebate. Tax tickets are purchased for one million yuan, and the Tianjin factory obtains them from Shanghai for affixing. Since receiving the notice from the Unified Tax Bureau of the Four Provinces, Krisson, the manager of the Tianjin factory, immediately reported to the Shanghai headquarters and requested intervention from the Tianjin British Consulate. However, the Unified Tax Bureau limited the factory to paying taxes according to regulations within five days, otherwise, the goods would be prohibited from leaving the factory. On the afternoon of the 3rd, a large number of armed police were sent to surround the entire factory, demanding that the factory comply. Later, the British Consul went to mediate, praying that the Shanghai factory's telegram would arrive before replying. Currently, the factory has directly negotiated with the Ministry of Finance. The factory here is temporarily maintaining work. The British manager stated that if it is absolutely impossible, there is only bankruptcy and dismissing the workers. When that time comes, 2,000 unemployed men and women will increase social unrest. The authorities may ease their attitude and not insist that taxes must be paid locally. However, this observation may be wrong. The authorities' will is very firm, and they may not let go if it is not complied with. (5th)

Wuxi: The Price Problem Resolved 69

Ji Kuan, the director of the Chief Committee of the Jiangsu Province Silkworm Industry Improvement Management Committee, came to Wuxi from Wujiang the day before yesterday to inspect the silkworm and silk testing ground. He also invited Li Baiping, the director in charge of preparations for the county's farmers' association, and County Magistrate Long, the director of the silkworm farming model district, Zhou Yuanquan, to the county government to discuss the issue of raising silkworm prices. Leading figures in the silk industry, Xue Shouhuan and Kuang Zukang, also went to meet the committee members one after another. Mr. Xue also expressed his acceptance of the government's goodwill and his willingness to sacrifice. Silkworms of excellent quality will be further increased appropriately. Yesterday, the silk industry association sent letters to various silkworm purchasing manufacturers to inform them. According to Hua Shaochun, the executive director of the silkworm industry association, they will also find ways to increase the price of silkworms within the possible range. At the same time, the committee members invited various silkworm seed field owners from Suzhou and Wuxi, including Lu Zirong, Shao Shenpei, and Zhu Youfu, to the Wuxi Hotel to discuss the distribution of the number of autumn silkworm seeds to be transported to Zhejiang Province. As a result, Zhejiang Province needs 400,000 sheets of autumn silkworm seeds from other provinces this year, of which 75,000 sheets will be allocated by the Central Silkworm and Silk Testing Ground, and 325,000 sheets will be supplied by Jiangsu Province. Of this number, 200,000 sheets will be allocated to fields in Zhenjiang, 100,000 sheets to fields in Suzhou, and 25,000 sheets to fields in Wuxi. Yesterday (the 6th) at noon, the committee members left Wuxi for Shanghai to discuss important matters.

Also, the silk factory guild in this county recently received instructions from the Jiangsu Provincial Silkworm Industry Improvement Management Committee and issued the following regulations regarding the fees for semi-dried silkworms: 1. All semi-drying silkworm stores must register in advance and be approved by the district. 2. Silkworm purchasers who do not operate silk factories are not allowed to semi-dry. 3. Semi-dried silkworms must still be weighed, and the price will be converted to 70% of the price of fresh silkworms for fee payment. 4. If it is found that fully dried silkworms are being passed off as semi-dried silkworms, they will be confiscated. 5. The district will send personnel to inspect the circulation of semi-dried silkworm stores' joint tickets and code tickets. 6. Semi-dried silkworms must still pay fees to obtain a permit before they can be transported. The number of baskets and the net weight of semi-dried silkworms must be noted on the fee payment certificate for each shipment, and the permit number must be noted on the transport permit. After receiving the order, the guild sent letters to various silk factories yesterday to be followed. A total of 204 silkworm stores are registered in this county, with 2,690 single stoves. There are also 47 unqualified silkworm stores in various townships leased by cooperatives that have already been sealed, and 130 single stoves and 4 double stoves are registered with the model district. Yesterday (the 6th), all silkworm stores in the city and countryside opened to purchase silkworms. The price of silkworms in the city area was 32 yuan per dan, and the goods were not enthusiastic. In the Changda Mansion area of the rural area, improved silkworm seeds were baked and dried by cooperatives, totaling about sixty or seventy dan, so the fresh silkworms collected by various silkworm stores yesterday were all inferior goods, and the price was 33 yuan per dan. In the towns of Dongfangqian and Bashiqiao, the arrival of goods at the silkworm stores was also not enthusiastic, and the price was 35 yuan to 32 yuan per dan. There are a total of four silkworm stores in Dongting Town, and the arrival of goods was still enthusiastic, with the highest price seen at 34 yuan per dan. Silkworm stores in Guzhou, Yuqi, and Beiqifang have also opened for purchase, with the price at 35 yuan per dan, and the quality is very good. Silkworm stores in Jiangyin will open for purchase today (the 7th). Silkworm stores in Liyang began purchasing on the 4th, but they are all local silkworms, with a price of 21 yuan per dan.
