Jiangyin: Zhenjiang Customs Branch Seizes Smuggled Sugar 71

The Jiangyin branch of the Zhenjiang Customs found a sailboat passing through Huangtiangang port the day before yesterday afternoon. It seized twenty bags of sugar transported from Wuxi to Rugao. Because there was no transport permit, there was suspicion of smuggling, and the boat was immediately seized. A sample was sealed and sent to the Zhenjiang Customs for inspection before further processing.

Changzhou: Inspector Ding Visits Changzhou for Inspection 72

Ding Chao Wu, a Central Committee member and also Jiangsu Provincial Supervisory Commissioner, set out from Zhenjiang on the morning of the 5th with his secretary Jiang Yulin, section chief Huang Sen, investigation members Zhang Ji, Xu Changrui, and guards in two private cars. They first arrived in Danyang for inspection, and left Danyang for Jintan for inspection at 2:00 PM. At around 4:00 PM, they arrived in Changzhou by car along the Wu Li Road and stayed at the Dacheng Hotel. Local officials heard the news and came to pay their respects. Inspector Ding then toured Tianning Temple and the First Park. On the morning of the 6th, he went to various agencies for inspection. In the afternoon, he planned to go to Guanxing and Liyang for inspection. Within the next few days, he may go to Changshu to inspect water conservancy projects before returning to the province.

Changshu: The Zinan Case Will Be Expanded 73

Kuang Zinan, a local resident and second-class pilot who had just returned from studying in Japan, was invited to a feast by relatives and friends on the second day of his return to Changshu. On the way home, he suddenly had a quarrel with a certain woman. He reported to the First Branch of the Public Security Bureau but was mistakenly identified as a rioter and was tied up and beaten, suffering serious injuries. Knowing that this was unfavorable, the branch itself destroyed a portion of its belongings, claiming that he had destroyed public property. This case has caused public outrage and has been transferred to the judiciary for investigation. Because Kuang Zinan's brother was charged with destroying public property, he was released on bail for 1,000 yuan. This matter has been brought to the attention of the Aviation Alumni Association in Japan. Chen Dejian, Fang Wenxin, Weng Shanggong, Gao Wenxiao, Yang Qianren, Li Youmao, and Yang Beichao have jointly launched assistance, telegraphed to national aviation groups for support, and published an advertisement applying for justice to be upheld by people in this county. It is generally expected that this case will be expanded.

Hangzhou: Night Buses on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway 74

Since the operation of passenger cars on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway, travel has been very convenient. Now, the First District Management Office of the Zhejiang Provincial Highway Department is planning to increase its business by adding a night bus service on that road. It has ordered chassis from the manufacturer and the repair shop is assembling a new sleeper car, which can accommodate twelve passengers. The bedding is quite exquisite. It will depart every night at 12:00 AM and arrive in Shanghai at 6:00 AM the next morning. The fare is 6.2 yuan per passenger. It will be put into operation after being submitted to the Construction Department for approval.

International Problems Research Association Held its Fourth Annual Meeting Yesterday: Foreign Minister Zhang Delivers a Detailed Speech on International Issues and the Association's Mission 75

The International Problems Research Association held its fourth annual meeting yesterday evening at 6:00 PM at the International Hotel. Foreign Minister Zhang Qun, Soviet Ambassador Bogomolov, Japanese Chargé d'Affaires Wakasugi, and consuls-general from various countries in Shanghai were invited, totaling over 300 guests and hosts, making for a grand occasion. During the meeting, Foreign Minister Zhang delivered a speech emphasizing the importance of paying special attention to international issues, the Association's adaptation to these needs, and its responsibilities. The details are as follows:

Distinguished Guests Attending: The members and guests who attended last night included Foreign Minister Zhang Qun, Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi, Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs Chen Jie, Director of the Intelligence Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Li Dijun, Secretary of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Duan Maolan, Soviet Ambassador Bogomolov, Japanese Chargé d'Affaires Wakasugi, Swedish Chargé d'Affaires Freijs, Swiss Chargé d'Affaires Laudi, Soviet Consul-General Spielberg, Italian Consul-General Nylon, Belgian Consul-General Teilvo, Portuguese Consul-General Feile, Brazilian Consul-General Blaiko, Polish Consul-General Krzystynsky, Finnish Consul-General Niekanlai, as well as Li Shizeng, Liu Hongsheng, Qian Xinzhi, Wang Xiaolai, Cai Wuji, Li Zhaohuan, Bei Songsun, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Huang Yanpei, Xu Ji, Guo Shun, Zhao Jinqing, Xu Peihuang, Dai Enji, and their spouses, totaling over 300 people. Cao Yunxiang, acting chairman of the board, presided over the meeting.

Chairman's Report: Chairman Cao Yunxiang began by reporting on major international events of the past year, stating that the international situation had been developing rapidly, with complex and multifaceted diplomatic maneuvers. It was impossible to cover everything in a few words. However, by observing the past, one could understand the future, and the following major events could guide future actions. The following matters, without international cooperation, would inevitably be sources of future wars. Briefly, these included economic competition arising from raw materials and markets, the expansionist desires of Italy and Japan, the brewing of political wars in South America, the actions of Balkan and Near Eastern countries as leaders, leading to the involvement of several European nations, the visible and hidden dangers of communism, the increase in German military preparations, and the collapse of international justice and morality. Therefore, the future fate of the world may be influenced by the above-mentioned facts and international suspicions. We cannot ignore these trends. Due to time constraints, he would only present the most important international events of the past twelve months. On July 1st, the Soviet Union warned Japan due to border conflicts. On the 25th, the world paid attention to Italian-Albanian relations and the situation in North China. On August 16th, Eden and Laval met in Paris to discuss granting Italy economic priority in Albania as a basis for peace, but without result. On the 21st, the German manager of the South Manchurian Railway requested the establishment of a subsidiary company with a capital of 200 million Japanese yen to develop the economy of North China. On September 11th, British Foreign Secretary Hoare, French Prime Minister Laval, and Soviet Ambassador Litvinov declared in Geneva their commitment to maintaining the League of Nations. Britain dispatched warships to the Mediterranean. On the 18th, Italy issued 7 billion lira in war bonds. On the 19th, Sir Ross came to the Far East to investigate the possibility of economic cooperation. On October 3rd, Italian troops invaded Albania. On the 7th, the League of Nations recognized Italy's aggression. On the 20th, Yugoslavia and Turkey signed a friendship and non-aggression treaty. On the 31st, President Wang was assassinated in Nanjing. On November 3rd, China reformed its currency system. On the 15th, Quezon was elected President of the Philippine Republic, which would formally become independent after ten years. On the 18th, various countries jointly decided not to buy Italian goods and not to sell important products to Italy. On December 6th, the British and American foreign ministers declared their opposition to Japan's actions in North China. On the 7th, the "China Clipper" airplane crossed the Pacific for the first time. On the 9th, representatives of eleven countries gathered in London to begin negotiations to conclude a new naval treaty. On the 12th, the U.S. reduced silver purchases, and world silver prices fell. On the 17th, the Council of the League of Nations declared that it did not approve of the peace terms proposed by Britain and France to Italy. On January 15th, Japan's request for naval equality was rejected, and it withdrew from the London Naval Disarmament Conference. On the 22nd, Japan protested the Sino-French aviation agreement. On the 28th, the U.S. Tariff Commission announced that U.S. exports to Japan exceeded Japanese exports to the U.S. On February 10th, the U.S. Senate impeached Pittman for attacking Japan's policy in China. On the 15th, Tokyo announced a flight plan to Luo Pan Gu. On the 20th, moderate factions prevailed in the Japanese general election. On the 26th, a small group of officers murdered four moderate politicians and then surrendered unconditionally to the palace guards. On March 7th, Italy and Abyssinia expressed willingness to negotiate peace. Hitler moved 40,000 troops to the Rhineland. On the 8th, France declared that it would not open negotiations with Germany until German troops withdrew from the Rhineland. On the 10th, Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota, on behalf of the Prime Minister, declared that there would be no war during his term. On the 21st, the Communist army invaded Shanxi. On the 24th, Italy, Austria, and Hungary signed a trade agreement, with rumors of an undeclared military annex. On the 25th, the U.S., Britain, and France concluded a naval treaty, requiring each signatory to notify other countries before building warships and inviting Japan and Italy to join the treaty. On the 29th, 45 million members of the German Nazi Party voted to support Hitler. On April 5th, Japanese Ambassador to China Arita was ordered to return home to become Foreign Minister. On the 7th, Italian troops entered the Albanian capital, marking the final phase of the Italian-Albanian war. Smuggling in North China was rampant, resulting in annual tax revenue losses of 30 to 100 million. Japan demanded that the Nanyuan barracks be used for stationing Japanese troops.

Foreign Minister's Speech: Foreign Minister Zhang then delivered a speech, stating, "The International Problems Research Association is holding its fourth annual meeting today. Distinguished Chinese and foreign guests and members of the Association are gathered together. I am honored to participate in this grand occasion. Your Association is composed of well-known figures from society, including university presidents, writers, and bankers. It is an academic organization dedicated to the study of international issues. Such organizations exist in various countries. For example, in Britain, there is the Royal Institute of International Affairs; in the United States, there is the Council on Foreign Relations; and in Japan, there are the Japan International Association led by Mr. Ishii and the Japan Foreign Affairs Association led by Mr. Yoshizawa. Other countries also have similar organizations, similar in nature to your association. It is a very prestigious academic group and can be said to be a tool for exercising people's diplomacy. In recent decades, transportation has become exceptionally advanced. The ancient dream of shrinking the earth, the so-called 'ten thousand miles as if in one's courtyard,' has been fully realized. As a result, international relations, whether in culture, politics, or economics, are becoming increasingly complex day by day. There is a state of mutual dependence among various ethnic groups in all aspects of life. For example, in the past, merchants could ignore international news and conduct their own business. However, the situation is different now. Fluctuations in international exchange rates immediately affect the cost of goods, so merchants must pay attention to international news. 'A single hair can move the whole body' is a perfect way to describe the complex international relations of today. Since international relations are becoming more complex day by day, our understanding of international affairs is becoming increasingly necessary. In recent years, the trend of researching international issues in our country has been developing. In academic circles, universities have added courses on international relations. In publishing, publications discussing diplomacy and international issues are also increasing. Even local newspapers, which often did not carry international news twenty years ago, are now paying attention to international news, whether political or economic. This is a good phenomenon, but to gain a full understanding of complex international issues and conduct comprehensive research, it is necessary to concentrate talent, organize groups, and use a division of labor and cooperation. Your association has emerged to meet this need. In the past four years, it has achieved remarkable results. We can believe that it will make even greater contributions to the country and society in the future. Regarding the methods of researching international issues, the members have rich experience, and I need not say more. However, in addition to studying international issues, your association also has the mission of people's diplomacy. To accomplish this mission, we must focus on mutual understanding among nations, because the relationship between countries is the same as the relationship between people. We know that humans are emotional animals, so people must connect emotionally to increase friendship. General social disputes arise in four stages: isolation leading to misunderstanding, misunderstanding leading to suspicion, and suspicion leading to conflict. International disputes are also the same. Therefore, if citizens of various countries can interact and communicate with each other, isolation will not arise. Once isolation is gone, all misunderstandings, suspicions, open and covert struggles can naturally be eliminated. Moreover, we humans also have a supreme common goal, which is international peace. Our country, for thousands of years, has been a country that emphasizes integrity and loves peace. Our national policy can be summarized in one sentence: seek self-preservation domestically and coexistence internationally. The key to coexistence is peace. To implement this policy, we must work together both officially and privately. Governments should respect each other's sovereignty and cooperate sincerely, and citizens should reciprocate and communicate with each other to remove isolation, explain misunderstandings, and eliminate suspicion, so as to establish a foundation for international peace. The members here have a deep understanding and thorough knowledge of current international affairs. Various countries also have similar organizations, so we can naturally communicate with each other, enhance friendship among citizens, and promote international cooperation. Today's harmonious atmosphere fully demonstrates your association's efforts and the sincere sympathy and enthusiastic support of the guests. Success in the future can be predicted. I would like to raise a glass and wish all members and guests good health." (The speech was translated into English by Secretary Duan Maolan.) Then, Soviet Ambassador Bogomolov and Japanese Chargé d'Affaires Wakasugi delivered speeches. The guests and hosts enjoyed themselves, and the event ended at about 9:00 PM. Foreign Minister Zhang took the night express train to Beijing that evening.

Thirteen Fish Shops and the Fish Market Begin Cooperative Business: Special Facilitation for Market Entry Yesterday, Same Treatment Under All Market Regulations 76

The Shanghai Fresh Fish Industry Association's members, Ganfeng and thirteen other fish shops, have resolved their entanglement with the Shanghai Fish Market through the advice of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and the Ningbo Native Place Association. The cooperative agreement was finalized at a joint meeting of the Fish Market Board of Directors and the thirteen fish shops the night before last. They entered the market yesterday and began business immediately. The details are as follows:

Cooperation Agreed: The Shanghai Fish Market Board of Directors and Ganfeng and thirteen other fresh fish shops held a joint meeting the night before last, chaired by Chairman Du Yuesheng. Both parties openly and honestly negotiated, and unanimously passed the resolution for Ganfeng and the thirteen other fish shops to join the fish market. The measures were as follows: 1. The thirteen fish shops would abide by the fish market's business regulations and all rules. 2. The fish market would treat the thirteen fish shops that joined later the same as those who joined earlier. 3. All thirteen fish shops would have fish market brokers, one for each shop, totaling thirteen.

Business This Morning: Ganfeng, Shengji, Gongda, Qiafeng, Xiangshun, Dacheng, Dechang, Hongyuan, Gongshun, Yuantong, Taichang, Yuanyu, Hongchang, and the other thirteen fresh fish shops, after agreeing to cooperate with the fish market, went to the fish market yesterday morning to arrange everything, obtain entry and exit permits, and complete various procedures. At the same time, the fish market specially facilitated the entry procedures for the thirteen fish shops. Most of them moved in last night and were allowed to start business in the fish market this morning. A few others were unable to complete the procedures in time, so they would enter the market today and could open for business tomorrow morning. As for the old site at the 16th Pier, it would cease operations.

Same Treatment: Previously, eight fish shops had joined the fish market. This time, thirteen fish shops joined the fish market. All are market brokers. However, the market regulations stipulate that there are only two wholesalers, one for river fish and one for fresh fish. Huang Zhensheng is in charge of foreign fish. Previously, the eight shops that joined earlier requested priority rights. After Chairman Du Yuesheng and Director Yu Qiaqing persuaded the eight shops, they withdrew their request. The cooperative agreement of the thirteen fish shops was not easy to reach. In the future, with joint cooperation, the business development of the fish market can be predicted to be bright.

Telegram to the Ministry: The Ningbo Native Place Association in Shanghai telegraphed Minister Wu of the Ministry of Industry yesterday afternoon, stating, "To Minister Wu of the Ministry of Industry, Nanjing: Your esteemed telegram received. After repeated persuasion, all fish shops have agreed to cooperate and are allowed to join the market today. Respectfully reported, Yu Qiaqing and others of the Ningbo Native Place Association in Shanghai."

Misunderstandings Cleared: A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency visited Mr. Wang Xiaolai, General Manager of the Fish Market, yesterday. According to him, the fish market welcomed the joining and cooperation of the thirteen fish shops. After the open and honest negotiations at yesterday's (i.e., the day before yesterday) joint meeting, all previous misunderstandings had been completely cleared. The thirteen fish shops would cooperate and do business in accordance with the fish market's regulations. The fish market would treat the thirteen fish shops equally and decided to provide special facilitation, allowing them to enter the market for business before the joining procedures were completed. They had already moved in and were allowed to start business tomorrow morning (i.e., this morning). Currently, the fish market's business has increased to 50,000 yuan per day. It is predicted that during the fishing season in the next few days, it can increase to 70,000 yuan.

The Chamber of Commerce Cables to Request Inspection of Smuggled Artificial Silk: If Silk Fabrics Made from It Are Transported to Shanghai, Separate Audit Measures Should Be Established 80

Yesterday, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce requested the Ministry of Finance to establish separate audit measures for smuggled artificial silk used to make fabrics transported to Shanghai, cabling to the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing as follows: "To the Esteemed Ministry of Finance in Nanjing: On the 5th of this month, we received a letter from the Silk Fabric Industry Association stating, 'We have received a letter from Sheng Daze stating that the problem of domestic smuggling is becoming increasingly serious. Although the Ministry of Finance has issued orders to investigate and prohibit it, the reasons are complex and difficult to implement, and no effective results have been achieved. Recently, we have found that a large amount of tax-evaded artificial silk fabrics from Zhoucun in Shandong and Gaoyang in Tianjin are transported to various provinces. From Zhoucun alone, up to 5,000 to 6,000 bolts are transported to Shanghai daily by express train, completely made of artificial silk and interlaced silk-cotton products, and artificial silk and genuine silk interlaced products, so that the taxed products of Shanghai silk merchants cannot be sold and business is plummeting. If we do not take immediate action to stop this, the number of unemployed workers will exceed tens of thousands, and the future consequences are unimaginable. We have heard that the Ministry of Finance has measures to transport goods based on the Yunjian system, but the measures are not thorough enough and there are concerns that more malpractices will arise. Our association believes that unless we rely on the simple transfer of raw material dispatch orders, we will not be able to stop smuggling. If we only rely on the certification of local commercial groups, the effect will be weak. We should request the Ministry of Finance to send personnel to be stationed permanently in the areas with the most rampant smuggling, to conduct strict inspections, and order them to conscientiously implement the methods suggested by our industry, in order to protect legitimate merchants and protect the national silk industry. We are sending this letter to request your attention and to forward it to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce to be forwarded to the Ministry of Finance for consideration and handling.' We are now urgently informing you of this situation and respectfully request your esteemed chamber to consider it and approve its forwarding, as we deeply appreciate it. We have found that after the tax-evaded artificial silk mentioned by the association is unloaded in a certain place, it is made into silk fabrics or silk-cotton interlaced products. In an instant, it has changed from imported smuggled goods to re-exported domestic goods. All these opportunistic situations cannot be prevented by the current provisions of the Interim Regulations on the Inspection and Marketing of Imported Goods. The association's statement that, at the time of re-export, artificial silk tax bills should be used to exchange for silk fabric transport permits is indeed to supplement the omissions in the regulations and to prevent opportunistic behavior. Although one is applied to imported foreign goods and the other is applied to re-exported domestic goods, the scope seems to be slightly expanded. However, at this time when smuggling is rampant and fraud is rampant, the country has one more inspection method, that is, the tax revenue has one less worry about smuggling. This matter is automatically requested by the industry and there is no hindrance. We should truthfully transmit the situation to your esteemed department for consideration, and if you approve its adoption and implement it immediately, it will be a public convenience. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce respectfully pleads."

Statistics on Shanghai Goods Exported to the United States for the First Five Months of This Year: Total Value of US$9,834,564 81

The U.S. Consul General's Office in Shanghai released statistics on Friday, stating that the total value of exports from Shanghai to the United States and U.S. territories in the first five months of this year was US$9,834,564. However, 12,475,450 ounces of silver, with a total value of US$5,582,764, are not included in this figure. Shanghai's exports to the United States in May were approximately US$1,400,000, of which sesame accounted for US$96.49 and tung oil accounted for US$134,936, bringing the total value of inedible plant products shipped to the United States in the five months to US$2,633,500. Textiles, including waste cotton, lace, embroidered cloth, carpets, wool, human hair, raw silk, waste silk, and straw hats, were worth a total of US$2,086.78. In addition, the value of tungsten shipped to the United States this year was US$396,580. In the first five months of this year, the Philippines purchased raw eggs, ham, peanut oil, soybeans, melon seeds, cotton wadding, cotton yarn, and other miscellaneous goods, totaling US$635,773, with US$101,789 in May. In May, Hawaii only purchased silk products and woodenware, worth US$9.952.

Shanghai Lawyers Association Holds Grand Meeting Today for the Unjust Imprisonment Compensation Movement Week, Expanding Publicity on the Significance of Unjust Imprisonment Compensation, Promoting Government to Enact the Unjust Imprisonment Compensation Law 83

Time... Today at 2:00 PM

Location... Tianhou Palace Chamber of Commerce

The Unjust Imprisonment Compensation Movement Committee of the Shanghai Lawyers Association has scheduled the Second Sports Meeting of the Unjust Imprisonment Compensation Movement Festival for 2:00 PM this month on the 7th (today), at the City Chamber of Commerce. At the same time, leaders from various sectors of the city will be invited, and all members of the Lawyers Association will be notified to attend. In recent days, the preparatory committee has been dividing up the work to carry out all preparatory matters, in addition to sending members to various radio stations to give speeches on the significance of unjust imprisonment compensation, and showing slides in various cinemas to expand publicity, so as to promote the government to enact the unjust imprisonment compensation law as soon as possible to protect human rights. The association's declaration and telegrams to the Capital's Judicial Yuan and the courts are recorded below:

Collecting Materials

The Shanghai Lawyers Association informs all members to solicit materials on unjust imprisonment. If you have seen or heard of anything, please collect it and present it at the meeting for submission to the general assembly for discussion.

Radio Speeches

The publicity committee has assigned a list of committee members to give speeches at various radio stations: Zhang Shijie at Chang Radio Station, time 6:00 PM; Mao Yun at Huaxing Radio Station, time 8:00 PM; Qin Liankui at Youlian Radio Station, time 8:00 PM; Shi Liang at Zhongxi Radio Station, time 8:00 PM; Wu Zhengwei at Guohua Radio Station, time same as above; Qian Jianqiu at Huaxing Radio Station, time same as above; Zhu Fu at Dongfang Radio Station, time same as above; Chen Zhi at Donglu Radio Station, time same as above; Yuan Yangan at Ligong Radio Station, time same as above; Yan Yinwu at Shanghai Radio Station, time same as above.

Declaration

The Shanghai Lawyers Association issued a declaration for the Second Unjust Imprisonment Compensation Movement Week, stating: The unjust imprisonment compensation movement originated five years ago at the Third Congress of the Republic of China Lawyers Association held in Hangzhou. At that time, the Congress passed a proposal on "Implementing a National Compensation Responsibility System for Government Errors in Judgment," which was submitted to the government but remained unanswered. In the twenty-second year, the Fifth Congress of the Association convened in Qingdao, and at the suggestion of this Association and the Wu County and Hang County Associations, it was proposed to the Legislative Yuan to formulate an unjust imprisonment compensation law. This was unanimously passed by the Congress, but the central government ignored it as before. When the Association held its Sixth Congress in Guangzhou, the cradle of the revolution, it was deemed necessary to expand publicity and begin a planned movement, passing a resolution to "Organize an Unjust Imprisonment Compensation Movement Committee." Since then, the committee has held regular meetings in various local associations on a rotating basis, making continuous efforts and appealing to public opinion. Finally, the highest authorities of judicial administration expressed that they would not ignore the people's due compensation for unjust imprisonment due to judicial economic difficulties, hoping to eliminate unjust imprisonment through unjust imprisonment compensation. At the same time, the Legislative Yuan's Legislative Committee also expressed extreme support for the entire Association's proposal (the full text can be found in the Association's Law Journal, Volume 3, Issue 3). Thus, the unjust imprisonment compensation movement received spiritual assistance from all levels of the country. It was resolved that the Lawyers Association in all parts of the country would choose a day in the first ten days of June each year to hold the unjust imprisonment compensation movement, in order to make a unified appeal across the country, awaken the deaf and enlighten the blind, and seek the early realization of the national compensation system. This is the origin of the Unjust Imprisonment Compensation Movement Week. Since the first national movement week was held last year, the national judicial conference, which has attracted the attention of the whole country and is full of expectations, has been held. This Association has seized the opportunity and, daring not to belittle itself, also presented the proposal "The Unjust Imprisonment Compensation System Should Be Realized Urgently" to the conference through its attending representatives in conjunction with lawyers' representatives from all over the country. After merging with the "Realize Unjust Imprisonment Compensation" proposal submitted by Guangzhou University for discussion, the resolution "The original proposal shall be sent by the Judicial Yuan to the Legislative Yuan" was obtained. This movement has relied on the concerted efforts of relevant people in the national judicial community to form an important legislative issue. The future publicity movement should be changed to supervise the legislative aspect to complete its mission, and to be as bright as the constitution to be implemented, which is an inevitable step. However, there are many causes of unjust imprisonment, and it is not easy to redress unjust imprisonment. Those who harbor grievances and bear injustice must have a strong and unyielding will and follow strict and cumbersome procedures in order to clear the clouds and see the blue sky. Even if they are fortunate enough to obtain compensation after being wronged, it is still not enough to cover one-tenth of the actual damage suffered. Those who are not firm in their will, submit to the established situation, seek to avoid increasing actual damage, and are willing to endure humiliation, weeping and swallowing their voices, and end their lives in injustice, are even more numerous. Law is intended to eliminate evil, but if used improperly, it will produce evil. Is it the fault of the system or the fault of people? Its shortcomings cannot be satisfied by merely talking about post-event compensation. It is necessary to first reduce the so-called unjust imprisonment. On the one hand, local poverty alleviation groups should be consulted so that the weak who harbor grievances without complaint and bear injustice and are suspected can obtain appropriate guidance and fully exert their defensive functions. On the other hand, the government should be urged to implement the habeas corpus law as soon as possible to reduce the causes of unjust imprisonment. As for the unification and independence of judicial power, and not allowing division or any political pressure, it is related to the country's policy of securing the state and pacifying the people, and it is not only to prevent the occurrence of unjust imprisonment. Therefore, the future direction of continued movement should be to attach equal importance to both post-event relief, and to pay more attention to various procedures for pre-event assistance and post-event compensation, and strive to make them simple, so as to avoid the establishment of empty systems. All systems will inevitably encounter difficulties due to resistance at the beginning of their creation. Unjust imprisonment compensation is also the same. In the past few years, this Association has worked with the Association and local lawyers' associations to jointly promote this movement, and has been encouraged by the sympathy of people of all walks of life. Although it has obtained the passage of a proposal at the national judicial conference and laid its foundation, judging from the current situation, the division of legal power is still the same, and the financial difficulties are even greater. Some people may regard this as a non-urgent matter, and others may be limited by the environment and aware of the difficulties, and discourage their courage to make a bold decision. However, we believe that a sound country must first protect the people. The constitutional government is about to be implemented. If there is no unjust imprisonment compensation system to assist it, then the so-called protection of human rights is only a cosmetic civilization. If people cannot protect their right to survival, what is the point of pacifying the country and resisting foreign aggression? At the holding of this movement week, we should resolutely express the minimum requirements, and promptly promote the completion of the unjust imprisonment compensation law, so that it can be implemented on the same day as the Constitution, in order to improve the organization and survival of the country. We respectfully inform the people of the country, and hope that we can work together to achieve it.

Telegrams to the Two Yuans

Telegrams to the Judicial Yuan and the Legislative Yuan, Nanjing Judicial Yuan and Legislative Yuan: Regarding the unjust imprisonment compensation system, countries in the East and the West have either made it a code or a precedent, and it has been implemented without hindrance for a long time. However, our country still lacks it. Years ago, the Republic of China Lawyers Association, in order to seek the realization of the unjust imprisonment compensation system, jointly drafted an unjust imprisonment compensation plan with local lawyers' associations and submitted it to request the formulation of laws and regulations. At the beginning of the movement, public opinion was in agreement. Last autumn, it was again submitted to the National Judicial Conference, and it was also resolved to ask the Judicial Yuan to forward it to the Legislative Yuan to formulate an unjust imprisonment compensation system as soon as possible. Under the current situation of a weak country and a weak legal system, it is urgently necessary to implement it in order to maintain the rule of law. Therefore, we telegraphically request Your Yuans to forward it to the Legislative Yuan to promptly formulate unjust imprisonment compensation laws and regulations to protect human rights and improve the organization of the country. We are extremely urgent and awaiting orders. Shanghai Lawyers Association bows respectfully.

Record of Major Events

A record of major events in the unjust imprisonment compensation movement is recorded below: In June of the 22nd year of the Republic of China, at the Fifth Congress of the Lawyers Association, the Shanghai Lawyers Association proposed that the Legislative Yuan immediately promulgate the unjust imprisonment compensation law, which was passed and forwarded to the government. In September of the 23rd year, at the Sixth Congress of the Lawyers Association, the Guangzhou Lawyers Association and others proposed the organization of an unjust imprisonment compensation movement committee. In November of the 23rd year, the Standing Committee hired 49 unjust committees and established a Standing Committee. On May 5 of the 24th year, the first unjust imprisonment compensation committee was held in Suzhou. On June 5 of the same year, the first national unjust imprisonment compensation movement was held. On September 20 of the 24th year, the judicial conference passed the unjust imprisonment compensation bill and sent it to the Legislative Yuan for formulation. In October of the same year, the Legislative Yuan replied to the Association that it had been submitted to the Criminal Law Committee for reference. On November 15 of the same year, a petition was submitted to the Fifth Plenary Session of the National Congress. On February 17 of the 25th year, the third unjust imprisonment compensation meeting requested the Seventh Congress to continue to strive for it. On May 5 of the same year, Article 26 of the draft constitution had a clear provision for the national compensation system. On May 30 of the same year, the fourth unjust imprisonment compensation movement committee was held in Yangzhou. In addition, lawyers such as Yu Chengxiu, Ma Shouhua, and Cai Zhaohuang all wrote articles to expound the purpose of unjust imprisonment compensation.

An order was issued to the Hunan Provincial Department of Finance to abolish the production and sales tax case, and it is sincerely requested to review and order the immediate abolition of the tax. The telegram has been received and understood. In this case, according to the Chamber of Commerce's presentation of the same situation, it was stated that "the business tax is levied on the act. The member stores of the Chamber of Commerce re-manufacture and sell their goods, and it is not inappropriate to levy the business tax. As for the production and sales tax in Hunan Province, it was previously submitted to the court for an order to the Hunan Provincial Government to promptly stipulate measures for gradual abolition and report to the Ministry. The Chamber of Commerce's request to cancel the production and sales tax should be handled after the Hunan Provincial Government's report is received and reviewed." The Chamber of Commerce was notified on May 22 with Fu Zi No. 9547. Recently, the Hunan Provincial Government's consult was approved, stating that the production and sales tax levied in Hunan Province is now being gradually abolished in accordance with the court's order. It has been decided that starting from the 25th year, steps will be taken to abolish the tax, first exempting or reducing the tax rate on daily necessities for civilians. The above telegram is combined with the approval for your information. This approval.

President Mościcki of Poland

Polish President's Tenth Anniversary of Inauguration Celebrated by Polish Community in Shanghai, Polish Minister to Attend 84

Dr. Mościcki, the President of Poland, is a world-renowned great scientist and is therefore known as the Scientific President. In June 1926, he was elected as President, and in 1933, when his term expired, he was re-elected with the most votes in the Parliament, because even the opposition party unanimously supported his scholarship and ability to handle affairs. Today is the tenth anniversary of Mr. Mościcki's inauguration as President, and the Polish government and people are celebrating and congratulating him. The Polish community in Shanghai will hold a celebration meeting at the YWCA at 999 Jing'an Temple Road at 9:00 AM today. The Polish Minister Wei Dengshou and the Chairman of the Overseas Chinese Federation will give speeches, and a Polish band will perform music to add to the fun. Mr. Mościcki is now 69 years old. He studied in Warsaw in his childhood and then entered the Riga Industrial School, where he excelled. After graduation, he devoted himself to revolutionary work, seeking to reclaim Poland's right to independence under the violent rule of Imperial Russia, and was eventually forced to flee overseas. He first went to London and worked as the director of a chemical laboratory, where he met the late Polish national hero General Piłsudski and became close friends. The success of the Polish independence movement was based on this. Later, Mr. Mościcki served as a professor at various universities in Europe and made many amazing inventions. Although Mr. Mościcki is now the head of state, he has never forgotten his scientific research work. In addition to his political work, he is still immersed in the laboratory, conducting tireless research. His expertise is in inorganic chemistry, electrochemistry, and electrical physics. On December 7 last year, the 30th anniversary of Mr. Mościcki's successful chemical invention was celebrated, and heads of state and scientific research institutions from various countries sent telegrams to congratulate him, which was extremely prosperous. Mr. Mościcki has made remarkable achievements during his tenure as President, which are too numerous to mention. The main ones include the proclamation of the new constitution, the signing of non-aggression treaties with Germany and the Soviet Union, the strengthening of armaments, the completion of railways, highways, and transportation networks, the stability of currency, and the development of industry and commerce, which have made Poland increasingly strong. He is especially commendable for his selfless personality, which has reconciled his political enemies and moved them to repent.

Huge Execution Case Involving Over One Million, Li Guojie Released on Bail Yesterday, Imprisoned for Three and a Half Years, Family Property Neglected, Li Zanhhou and Yu Qiaqing Responsible for Bail 86

Li Guojie, the grandson of the late Qing Dynasty Minister Li Hongzhang and former general manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, when Chen Mingshu concurrently served as the Minister of Communications and Chen Fumu served as the Deputy Minister of Communications and concurrently the supervisor of the company, arbitrarily mortgaged four warehouses to the China Business Company and signed a contract with the Dalae Steamship Company that forfeited rights. Later, when Chen Mingqu and others failed, Zhu Jiahua, who was the Minister of Communications, discovered the illegal contract and found that 700,000 taels had been deducted as a commission when the contract was signed, which was said to have been taken by Chen Fumu. The contract was ordered to be canceled, so the 700,000 taels were unaccounted for. Therefore, the Ministry of Communications consulted the Ministry of Judicial Administration to send Li to the Shanghai District Court for trial. Because Li suffered from a chronic disease, the court, in order to restrict his residence, had Lawyer Jiang Yiping and Fuchang Ginseng Firm act as guarantors to send him to live in the first-class ward of Shanghai Hospital. The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau Inspectorate sent police officers to investigate, and the court sent bailiffs to guard him. The prosecutor filed a public prosecution for breach of trust and embezzlement. The first instance sentenced Li Guojie to three years of imprisonment. Li refused to accept the sentence and appealed. The First Criminal Court of the Jiangsu Higher Court came to Shanghai for trial and increased the sentence to three years and six months and ordered him to return 700,000 taels of damage to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, plus interest. Li appealed to the Supreme Court of the Third Instance, which recently ruled to revoke the original judgment and change the sentence to eight months of imprisonment for Li Guojie, with a two-year reprieve. The number of days of detention was also allowed to be offset, so the criminal case has ended. Li Guojie could have regained his freedom, but in the private prosecution part, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company re-engaged Lawyer Jiang Hechun to file a petition with the District Court for execution and recovery. Yesterday, Judge Xu Hongxi of the Execution Division opened a court to interrogate him. He was taken to Li Guojie at Shanghai Hospital. At 10:00 AM, Judge Xu opened the Fourth Court to interrogate him. After Jiang Hechun, the attorney for the plaintiff creditor China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, reported to the court, Jiang Yiping and Lu Shifang, the attorneys for the defendant debtor Li Guojie, also reported to the court. The judge ordered the debtor Li Guojie to be brought to court and asked, "The 700,000 taels that you embezzled, plus interest, has now become more than 1.2 million. All your property should be reported so that it can be executed." He replied, "I have been imprisoned for three and a half years, and I have not had time to take care of my family property, so I am very unfamiliar with it. Therefore, I request permission to be released on bail, and I will naturally sort it out." At this point, the defendant's attorney rose and requested that Li be handed over to a guarantor who can be summoned at any time. Now, the prominent official and businessman Li Zanhhou and Yu Qiaqing are acting as guarantors, hoping that the case can be resolved as soon as possible. At this point, the plaintiff's creditor attorney rose to object, claiming that the amount involved in this case was too large, and the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company authorities had a great responsibility, so they reported it to the Ministry of Communications. Therefore, before obtaining an order from the Ministry, he still requested that Li Guojie be detained. The defendant's attorney retorted that the criminal part of Li Guojie's case had ended, and that even if he was detained for a long time, it would not be of any benefit to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. Moreover, after the debtor is released on bail and restores his social credibility, he can find ways to raise money, which is more than giving one more penny to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, which is more national currency for the country, which is a win-win situation. The judge said that it was noon and he needed to investigate the identities of the guarantors and their corresponding responsibilities. He ordered the hearing to continue at 2:00 PM. In the afternoon, Judge Xu returned to the court and summoned the guarantors Li Zanhhou and Yu Qiaqing to the court. He explained that if they guaranteed Li Guojie's release, they must be responsible for summoning him at any time. If he could not be summoned, then the guarantors would be responsible for all the debts. The guarantors agreed and wrote and signed the bail bond, granting Li Guojie bail. It was 3:30 PM.

National Physicians' Association Requests Selection of Practical Medical Talents, Health and Medical Facilities Are Biased Towards Urban Areas, Medical Needs in Rural Areas Are Difficult to Meet 87

The National Physicians' Association of this city, in view of the lack of practical physicians in the country and the fact that health and medical facilities are only biased towards commercial cities and cannot penetrate into the hinterland, so that the treatment of injuries and illnesses among the people is also deeply felt to be impossible to cope with, which is a major problem, and it is urgently necessary to conduct medical examinations to meet the needs. Yesterday, a special report was submitted to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Health, stating:

Petition for Medical Examination

of Practical Medical Knowledge

for the Benefit of Medical Administration

to Clearly State Views

and Humbly Request Consideration and Adoption

It is humbly submitted that in our country, with its vast territory and large population, new doctors in society are felt to be in short supply. In the past, in order to adapt to the national conditions and unify medical administration, the Ministry of Health, in addition to implementing the Physicians' Regulations, also formulated a flexible method for issuing certificates in August of the 21st year of the Republic of China, and issued general certificates, originally intending to

Relieve the Lack of Medical Talents

and Assist in Medical Administration. However, due to various factors such as time, region, and personnel, the results were neither universal, and the emergence of formal physicians, due to the small number of medical schools, was even more of a drop in the bucket. Therefore, public health and medical facilities, except for commercial cities, have not yet been extended to the interior. If this continues, it will not only greatly hinder the future of medicine, but also

the Treatment of Injuries and Illnesses Among the People

will be deeply felt to be impossible to cope with. Members of the Association are scattered throughout the country and have more real and accurate observations. This time, at the opening of the Fourth National Physicians' Representative Conference, there was a proposal to request Your Yuan (Ministry) to hold examinations for medical talents among those who have not been registered under the flexible certificate issuance method. The conference resolved to formulate the following examination methods:

Local Authorities of Various Provinces

together with academic organizations and professional organizations related to medicine, appoint experts to form specialized committees to investigate those new doctors across the country who have not graduated from formal medical schools, and issue licenses to practice medicine only after passing both basic medical science and clinical medicine. This practice

Examination Method

is held twice a year, in the spring and autumn, for both academic theory and clinical practice, as a supplement to the insufficient number of physicians. However, those who have graduated from correspondence schools in various places and have no practical experience are not included in this limit. When holding the examinations, the committee shall also join the provincial governments, education departments, provincial medical colleges, and provincial hospitals to form mobile medical teams,

go to various places

to be responsible for investigating and treating the unique responsibilities of each locality, and at the same time conduct on-site examinations for practitioners who have not obtained a license to practice medicine. Those who fail the examination will be given separate training in the location of each provincial government to supplement their knowledge. This method, although

is an Expedient Measure

can also be said to be a temporary remedy for the current situation of a lack of medical talent in the country. In accordance with the resolution of the Fourth National Congress of the Association, it is humbly submitted to Your Excellency for consideration and adoption. Whether it is appropriate or not, please decide, as it is for the public good. Sincerely submitted.

Kidnapping Attempt on Mr. Ye on Route Ghisi Failed, Incident Occurred at 12:00 Last Night, Thugs Opened Fire but Did Not Injure Anyone 88

Mr. Ye, the manager of the Continental Company, was driving his own car to his brother's house at No. 13, Lane 414, Route Ghisi in the French Concession at about 12:00 last night when something happened. Just as the car arrived at the entrance of the lane, three thugs ambushed in the dark rushed into the car, intending to kidnap him. Fortunately, Mr. Ye was unusually alert and knew that the newcomers were definitely not good people. He immediately ordered the driver to turn the car around, stepped on the gas, and drove away to the west, thus escaping the disaster. When the car escaped, the thugs fired two shots, but fortunately, no one was injured. Afterwards, Mr. Ye reported the incident to the local French police station. When the armed Chinese and Western detectives arrived at the scene of the incident, the bandits had already fled without a trace.

National Goods Movement Exhibition: Scheduled Lantern Parade 89

The National Goods Movement Exhibition of this city has been open for two weeks, and the sales of goods from various factories in the sales department have reached over 200,000 yuan. The number of visitors is increasing daily. In order to expand publicity, the association recently decided in a standing committee meeting to hold a National Goods Movement Lantern Parade on June 15th. All of the more than one hundred factories and businesses in the venue will participate. They have already applied to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for protection along the route during the event. Decorations and lanterns are being fully prepared. The details are recorded below:

Application for Protection Along the Route

The association has submitted a request to the Municipal Public Security Bureau, requesting instructions to the various branches in Shanghai South to provide protection along the route during the event. The submission is for holding the National Goods Movement Lantern Parade. Since the various public groups and organizations in this city designated this year as the National Goods Year for citizens, the association was formally established and registered with the Municipal Government and the Bureau of Social Affairs. Its sole purpose is to promote national goods and publicize domestic products. It has successively held events such as the National Goods Sample Trademark Exhibition, the Shanghai West National Goods Exhibition, and the Shanghai South Temporary Market to promote the national goods industry. Although it has worked hard for half a year, the results have been limited. This is because social customs have always favored foreign goods, and every year, huge amounts of money flow overseas, draining the country's resources and causing economic panic. To reverse this declining trend, a large-scale national goods movement is needed to awaken the people from their infatuation with foreign goods and to save the country and ensure its survival. The association, witnessing this situation, fears that the country will perish soon. Therefore, it is holding the Shanghai National Goods Movement Exhibition to promote the advancement of the national goods movement. In order to expand publicity, it plans to lead all the national goods factories and businesses in the association to hold a National Goods Lantern Parade on June 15th, hoping that the slogan of "everyone uses national goods" will be known to every household, understood by women and children, and permanently imprinted in the minds of the people, so as to achieve the goal of defeating foreign goods and preventing the outflow of wealth. However, this matter is of great importance. In addition to separately organizing a preparatory committee for the lantern parade to handle preparations, it has also prepared a document with a route map of the lantern parade, requesting your bureau to approve it and instruct the various branches in Shanghai South to provide the convenience of protection along the route at the time to ensure safety. This is deeply appreciated. Respectfully submitted to Cai, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, by the Shanghai Citizens' National Goods Year National Goods Movement Association.

Procedures for Participating in the Parade

Procedures for National Goods Factories to Participate in the National Goods Movement Lantern Parade:

* All factories and businesses participating in the National Goods Lantern Parade must be manufacturers or sellers of national goods.

* All kinds of lanterns and trademarks used by participating factories and businesses in the parade must be provided by themselves. In addition to sending personnel to accompany the parade and the necessary expenses, the factories and businesses shall bear all costs themselves and shall not pay any fees.

* Factories and businesses shall not distribute printed materials during the parade. However, if they have advertising flyers for their products, they must first have them stamped by the Bureau of Public Utilities one day in advance and must not engage in disorderly shouting or other actions.

* All personnel from the factories and businesses participating in the parade must obey the orders of the parade's general commander and take care along the route. The association will send letters to both the military and police to provide protection to prevent accidents.

* The date of the parade is set for June 15th (postponed in case of rain). The departure time is 7:00 PM. However, all participating personnel and lanterns from the factories and businesses must gather at Penglai Road two hours before departure for assembly and formation. Latecomers will not be waited for.

* Personnel from participating factories and businesses must line up according to the numbering provided by the association and must not push ahead or fall behind. They must not leave the parade midway. In case of special circumstances, they must obtain permission from the general commander before leaving.

* All participating factories and businesses must register at the association's office by the 12th of this month and confirm the number of participating personnel and collect participation certificates. The deadline will not be extended.

* The order of the parade numbers for participating factories and businesses will be based on the order of registration.

* All participating personnel carrying lanterns from the factories and businesses must walk along the parade route prescribed by the association and must not hire cars to ensure uniformity.

* All factories and businesses participating in the National Goods Exhibition are naturally participants in the Lantern Parade. Those who have not participated in the National Goods Exhibition but wish to join are welcome, but they must comply with the above procedures.

Route and Person in Charge

The parade route of the association has been decided. The assembly will be at Penglai Road in Xiaoximen. The parade will start from there, go south around Zhonghua Road and Minguo Road, circle the city wall once, and return to the association to disband. The standing committee meeting has appointed Liu Zhongying, Ge Futian, and Zheng Dongshan as the general commanders, and Ma Pingyuan, Wu Banjiang, Zhu Yunqing, Dai Qian, Fan Tianjin, Liu Mengfei, Wu Gechang, and Li Ruzhang as the eight inspectors. All of the more than 160 factories will participate. It is expected to cause a sensation among the people of Shanghai South and arouse enthusiastic attention.

Theft Case at Shanghai Local Court Solved; Three Stolen Guns Recovered; Liu Junqing's Investigation Leads to Discovery; Police Confirm Matching Serial Numbers; Traffickers Wang Xiao'a Yu and Wang Shi Arrested Together 91

The theft of twenty confiscated pistols and a wireless radio from the evidence vault of the Shanghai Local Court on the night of the 9th of last month caused a sensation in society. The court prepared documents consulting with various agencies for assistance. The Public Concession Police ordered all detectives to pay attention. Detective Liu Junqing of the Yulin Road Police Station began investigating criminals involved in arms trafficking. Suddenly, a person named Wang Xiao'a Yu was found trading pistols with Detective Liu's informant at a teahouse on Kunming Road, stating a price of seventy yuan for two pistols and thirty bullets. Upon the exchange of goods and money, the two pistols were brought, and Wang Xiao'a Yu was immediately arrested. Upon checking the serial numbers, it was confirmed that the pistols were the ones stolen from the Local Court. Under strict interrogation, Wang Xiao'a Yu confessed that an accomplice was hiding in a thatched shed at No. 55 Zhujiaqiao. The police rushed there and arrested a woman named Wang Shi, seizing six pistols. A total of eight pistols were seized. The serial numbers of the pistols are listed below. The serial numbers matching the stolen pistols from the Local Court are Nos. 3980, 3730, and 138988 (three pistols). The remaining are Nos. 2354, 2342, 1506, 12385, and 568294 (five pistols). As the case involved the interior, the suspects were transferred to the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau. After interrogation by the Third Section, they were ordered to be detained pending thorough investigation. The Local Court was notified to send personnel to identify the pistols for further handling.

Over Forty Trade Unions in This City Established a Restoration Organization Movement Yesterday; Established a Smuggling Reporting Committee; Sent Telegrams to Trade Unions Nationwide to Jointly Report Smuggling 92

Dagong News reports that trade unions in this city held a joint meeting last night to organize trade union organizations and assist the government in reporting smuggling. A Restoration of Trade Union Organizations and Smuggling Reporting Committee was established on the spot and will begin work immediately. A declaration has been issued. The details are as follows:

Joint Meeting

At 6 PM yesterday, a joint meeting of trade unions was held at No. 54 Ermalu, Shanghai Industrial Society. Representatives from over forty trades, including the Southern Goods Industry, Chinese and Foreign Textile Industry, Calligraphy and Fan Industry, Pharmaceutical Industry, Tea Industry, Canned Food Industry, Sauce Industry, Customs Brokerage Industry, Rice Industry, Porcelain Industry, Paper Industry, Silk Industry, Cosmetics Industry, Grocery Industry, Ham Industry, Silk Dyeing Industry, and Silk Industry, including Jiao Chunsheng, Zhao Zhenhua, Yu Yaoqiu, and over fifty others, attended.

Resolutions Passed

Yu Yaoqiu was elected as chairman. After formalities, the chairman reported on the situation of smuggling in North China, and the trade unions should assist the government in strictly reporting it. Then, discussions began.

* Regarding the determination of the organization's name, it was resolved to be named the Shanghai Municipal Trade Unions Restoration Organization Movement Committee.

* Regarding the drafting of the organizational regulations, it was resolved that Lu Muqin would draft them.

* Regarding the proposal to formulate measures for trade unions in various industries to report smuggling and request approval, it was resolved to amend and pass it.

* Regarding the proposal that the committee should issue a declaration and telegram to trade unions nationwide to jointly restore trade union organizations and effectively report smuggling, it was resolved to hand it over to the Secretariat for drafting.

Establishment of Two Committees

Two committees were immediately organized:

* The Shanghai Municipal Trade Unions Restoration Organization Movement Committee.

* The Shanghai Municipal Trade Unions Smuggling Reporting Committee. Cai Xiaohe, Jiao Chunsheng, Yuan Zhaoxin, Zhao Zhenhui, Lu Muqin, Yu Yaoqiu, and Shen Jiabin were elected as members to be responsible for handling the affairs of the two committees. Yang Jinlong was hired as secretary.

Declaration

Ever since the enactment of the Law on Industrial and Commercial Associations, it has been generally believed by the central legislative bodies and various ministries that the legal status of trade unions nationwide would not suffer any damage due to the transfer of the law. In fact, the fate of trade unions nationwide has long been in danger with the legal system. Looking at the current industrial and commercial associations, the employee members, who are hired by others, are rarely represented. Even if there are hundreds of millions of people, they are not allowed to participate. The past misfortunes have not been recognized by the central authorities. Although, I have heard that the organization of a nation is the measure of a country, and governing a state is governing its people. Labor-capital conflict is minor. The country is in imminent danger, and anyone who has ambition should take action to solve the problems. This is why Legislator Ma Yinchu proposed to overthrow the business organization and amend the law. The members of this committee, with years of worry, dare to exert our utmost effort to organize the Shanghai Municipal Trade Unions Restoration Organization Movement Committee and to organize a Smuggling Reporting Committee, formulating guidelines to assist the government. Since the purpose is pure and the measures are peaceful, it is hoped that all sectors of society will provide assistance, that the capitalists of each industry will remove misunderstandings, and that the trade unions nationwide will rise up to carry out this movement to save the country, to reverse the crisis, and to maintain the country. We solemnly declare this.

The Municipal Federation Opposes Japan Increasing Troops in North China; Telegrams Compatriots; Unite to Support the Government; and Telegraphs the Central Government to Protest Seriously 95

The Citizens' Federation of the First Special District of this city, considering that Japan is increasing troops in North China under the pretext of protecting its citizens, infringing upon our country's sovereignty, disrupting peace, and having a very significant impact, telegraphed the whole country yesterday and requested the central government to insist on resistance. The original telegram is recorded as follows:

Telegram to the Whole Country

Please, all newspaper offices, forward to all compatriots for public scrutiny. This time, Japan is unreasonably increasing troops in North China, adopting wartime establishment, occupying key positions, controlling transportation, destroying our country's sovereignty, and endangering peace in the Far East. Its arrogance is outrageous and infuriating. According to Japan's strong arguments, the pretexts for increasing troops are nothing more than protecting overseas citizens and following treaties. In fact, according to international practice, overseas citizens are naturally protected by the government of the country where they reside according to the law. If it is said that troops must be dispatched wherever overseas citizens travel, then how can such a phenomenon be tolerated in the international community? Take Japan, such as major cities such as Tokyo and Osaka, where many overseas citizens from other countries reside. Would other countries send troops to protect them, or even wield weapons like they are facing a formidable enemy? Would Japan not find this strange? If it is still claimed that public security in North China is precarious, then the bandits who invaded Shanxi have been defeated, and it is the instigation of who is causing anxiety today? Japan cannot deny its responsibility. Therefore, if Japan cannot reflect on itself and be aware of the wrongdoings, then the unreasonable increase of troops will only provoke emotions and threaten public security. Before it changes course, the future will be unbearable. As for invoking the Boxer Protocol to mask its aggressive troop increase, it is not worth refuting. The Boxer Protocol was signed more than thirty years ago. Over time, situations have changed, and it has long lost its effectiveness. Even stepping back, Sections 7 and 9 of the Protocol only allow a small number of troops to be stationed in Peiping and along the Peiping-Yulin railway to ensure the safety of the embassies. There are no words about deploying heavy troops to protect overseas citizens. Now Japan is increasing troops according to its original plan, which will soon be completed, and the Japanese and puppet troops along the Great Wall are also advancing south, taking a massive encirclement formation, and their actions are active. The purpose is obvious. Compatriots, since the September 18th Incident, the defenses of the Northeast have been completely removed, and now they are pressing closer, encroaching on our heartland. If we do not rise up and pursue them, the country will be fragmented, and sovereignty will be lost. This association has observed the difficult times and is extremely frightened. In addition to telegraphing the Central Government for serious negotiations, we respectfully ask all compatriots to rise up and support the government to protect the integrity of our territory and maintain national sovereignty. (Abbreviated below)

Request for Negotiations by Telegram

National Government of Nanjing, Executive Yuan, Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Military Affairs Commission, Japan is increasing troops in North China under various pretexts, infringing upon our sovereignty and threatening peace. It is outrageous and infuriating. Since the September 18th Incident, the defenses of the Northeast have been completely removed. Now they are oppressing our territory with strong troops and entering our heartland. If we do not take action, it will be difficult to survive. Therefore, we earnestly request serious negotiations to maintain national rights. We respectfully request you to examine and implement this. Sincerely, the Citizens' Federation of the First Special District of Shanghai.

The Inland River Navigation Association Requests Exemption from Tonnage Dues for Tugboats and Cargo Ships; The Executive Yuan Has Approved Reductions, Etc.; The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Specifically Notifies the Association 96

The Inland River Navigation Association of this city received a letter from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating: "In reply, on the 3rd of this month, we received the Executive Yuan Secretary-General's document No. 4056 dated June 2nd, quoting the President's instruction: 'Regarding the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce's submission on behalf of the Inland River Steamship Association that the collection of tonnage dues for tugboats and cargo ships in this city violates the law, listing various points, and requesting review and order to abolish it, the Ministry of Finance was instructed to review and reply. Regarding the claim in the original submission that Shanghai tugboats have licenses from the Ministry of Communications and have paid ship dues, and should not be charged dues again, the Ministry has revised the last paragraph of Article 2 of the Shanghai Municipal Ship Dues Regulations, specifically stipulating that ships holding nationality certificates or registered licenses issued by the Navigation Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications are exempt from inspection and may receive reduced fees. As these tugboats have been registered and licensed by the Ministry of Communications and have paid registration, license, and measurement fees, they can be charged reduced fees in accordance with the above regulations. The Ministry has also consulted with the Shanghai Municipal Government on the method of charging reduced fees for tugboats to alleviate the difficulties of navigation, etc.' The matter has been communicated to the original submitters for their information, etc.' We hereby inform you for your information." We checked that this case was submitted by your association, and we separately submitted it to the central government, and we further submitted the situation. We previously received a reply from the Central Political Conference, informing us that each case has been filed. Now, we respectfully request you to check and act accordingly."

Relief Society Investigator: Discover Two Abducted Women; Crime of Abduction Solved on Guangzhou Ship; Li Aizhen and Chen Aizhen Rescued 107

Yesterday at 11:00 AM, Chen Shaoting and Lin Yongfang, investigators from the China Relief Society for Women and Children, along with customs marine police detectives Qu Hequi, Zhou Zenghua, and Xu Juelu, went to the Taikoo Wharf in the French Concession to inspect the Guangzhou-bound ship about to set sail. In the steerage, they encountered three young women accompanied by a man wearing a blue cloth jacket and pants. The detectives noticed that while two of the women had permed hair and wore fashionable shoes and clothes, their arms were bare and their skin was very rough and dark, unlike people accustomed to living in the city. Suspicious, they began to question them. The four people spoke different dialects, revealing inconsistencies. They were taken to the marine police station. The man, named Chen Shunhai, 42 years old, from Lanxi, confessed to conspiring with his accomplice, Chen Haigen (still at large), to abduct the two fashionably dressed women and take them to Guangdong to open a brothel. Another woman arrested, named Pang Ereyuan, was Xu's concubine and was also accompanying them to Guangdong to avoid suspicion. According to Pang Ereyuan, 23 years old, from Changshu, her husband had passed away. Last year, she came to Shanghai from Xiju and was introduced to Xu Haigen by the defendant Chen Shunhai. They became lovers and lived at 304 Fumin Road in Nanshi. Chen brought the two abducted women there. When the incident occurred on the ship, Xu fled first. When questioned, one of the abducted women, Li Aizhen (also known as Su Feng), 19 years old, from Huzhou, said that two years ago, Chen Shunhai introduced her to Wang Aibin, a fellow villager, with whom she had been lovers for five or six months before breaking up. A month ago, Chen suddenly came to Huzhou, claiming that Wang had opened a ham shop in Guangdong and asked her to go to Guangdong to reunite with Wang. She believed him and came to Shanghai, staying at Xu Genhai's house, unaware that she was being deceived. The other abducted woman, Chen Aizhen (also known as Haizhen), 20 years old, from Zhenjiang, lived at 360 Fumin Road in Nanshi with her lover, Zhang Wen. She was lured by Xu Haigen and Pang Ereyuan, who said they would go to Guangdong for sightseeing, unaware that she was being forced into prostitution. The police officer stated that Chen's crime was premeditated and that the innocent women were almost thrown into a pit of fire, which was extremely hateful. He ordered that Xu be apprehended for further investigation.

Eight-Yuan Debt Leads to Murder: Body Examined Yesterday; Determined Cause of Death was Gunshot Wound; Ji Laoer Provides Information About Chen Xiangrong 110

Ji Laoer (also known as Amao, nicknamed Xiaochongming), from Nantong, residing at 24 Lanxin Lane, Boer Road, French Concession, borrowed eight yuan from Wu Caoshi, the wife of Suzhou resident Wu Agen, who lent money at high interest rates at 8 Rundenan Lane, Huanghe Road, in April of last year. At the time, Ji gave his gold ring to Wu as collateral for the eight yuan. Later, Ji was unable to repay the principal, so he converted the debt into a small interest loan, paying back 480 cash coins daily. Subsequently, Wu Agen and Wu Caoshi invited Ji to settle the interest at 54 Yihe Tea House, Huanghe Road, on the afternoon of the 4th, leading to a verbal dispute. The two parties agreed to meet at the same tea house the following afternoon to discuss the matter. When both sides arrived, the police were notified and dispatched detective Sun Qiwan to arrest them at the Yihe Tea House. He fired a warning shot, which struck Ji Shilin in the back, piercing his chest. Ji fled to the front of 8 Jialu Road, where he collapsed and died. After receiving the report, the police dispatched another detective to the scene and took Ji Laoer into custody to await the examination of the body. As reported yesterday, the police reported the matter to the Second Special Court. Prosecutor Wang Ren, forensic doctor Jiang, and secretary Peng arrived at noon to conduct the examination. Only the deceased's uncle, Ji Tinghua, arrived to claim the body for burial. The defendant, Ji Laoer, and the plaintiffs, Wu Agen and Wu Caoshi, and witness Chen Xiangrong were waiting in court for questioning and were not present. It was determined that Ji Shilin's death was caused by a gunshot wound, and Ji Tinghua took the body for burial. Subsequently, the police sent Ji Laoer to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special Court. Gu Shouxi, a lawyer from the police department, stated the case, claiming that the defendant attempted fraud and used an ax to injure a detective. The police department requested a seven-day extension for further investigation. Detective Xue Youlin then reported on the investigation and presented the murder weapon (an ax). Wu Agen, Wu Caoshi, and Chen Xiangrong testified that the defendant attempted fraud, injured a detective with the ax, and that the defendant's brother resisted the detective. The detective fired a warning shot, resulting in Chen Xiangrong's mistaken ax strike that killed Ji Shilin. Presiding Judge Wang Gangxu reviewed the testimony and decided to postpone the trial until the 13th. The defendant was returned to custody.
