申報 Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

Small Monographs

Critique of the "Latent Military Power Theory" 181

— Qing Jun

In 1931, the International Parliamentary Union, affiliated with the League of Nations, published a collection of essays entitled "How Will Future Wars Be?". This collection included articles by Professor Fried of France, General Menkil of Germany, Professor Aono of Japan, and others. They began to broadly raise the issue of "latent military power." Professor Fried's views can be said to be representative of this theory. His starting point was: "War depends on military power, and equally on economic and financial power." Therefore, he believed that economic and financial power plays a very important role in determining the outcome of a war. He first stated that his own research was limited to the economic elements of "latent military power," and therefore he avoided exploring "pure latent military power" and "spiritual and political latent military power."

Professor Fried believed that "pure latent military power" referred to "geographical location, the time and conditions for mobilizing national resources, the differences in manpower, armaments, and material components, the quality and education of the military, and other factors." As for "spiritual and political latent power," it referred to "the identity and unity of the residents, the disharmony of the system, and other factors." However, he considered both of these to be unimportant and did not study them specifically. In this way, he actually placed "economic latent power" outside of social relations and observed it separately from direct military factors. He considered "military and political latent power" to be "the research object of military technicians and politicians." He only paid attention to "economic latent military power" and divided it into three constituent parts: First, "the human element or demographic element." This latent power is A: "There should be many men between the ages of sixteen and sixty for military production, and the national composition of geographically concentrated production should be harmonious." B: "The stronger the residents' ability to restrain their own consumption, the greater this latent power will be." Second, "the technical element." This consists of A: agricultural productivity, B: raw materials and power resources, and C: industry and transportation. Third, "the economic and financial element": A: the burden capacity of the people, B: the country's borrowing power, and C: the ability to pay foreign debts.

Regarding Professor Fried's views, we believe that the first thing worth noting is that he believes that "political latent power" is the object of research for politicians and has nothing to do with his problem, but in the "human element" he proposed, he mentioned the importance of the national identity of the residents. This very obviously involved political factors, causing his research and his central argument to have irreconcilable contradictions.

Secondly, Professor Fried raised the issue of "the ability of residents to restrain their own consumption." But what determines this ability? He did not answer clearly. In fact, the so-called "ability of the people to restrain their own consumption" is not only an economic issue, but also a political issue. In capitalist countries, once a war breaks out, it is necessary to further restrict the consumption of the general working people and try to squeeze their blood and sweat to fill the war expenses. Such restraint of consumption is obviously not due to the wishes of the majority of the people, but is forcibly implemented with violence. As a result, the greater the power of this consumption restraint, the more the majority of the people will feel pain, the more they will ignite the spirit of resistance to this restraint and all oppression, and thus the more they will sharpen domestic contradictions, so as to weaken or even fundamentally eliminate its original external war-fighting ability. From this point of view, it can be seen that the so-called "ability to restrain consumption" is closely related to the political form of the country, and problems cannot be correctly concluded only by explaining the problem from the general economic situation.

Furthermore, the so-called "burden capacity of the people" is of great importance to war, but the problem cannot be decided by general measurement. Taking the general capitalist countries as an example, because power is concentrated in the hands of a few wealthy people, they will not only try to avoid their own many tax burdens during wartime, but also cleverly change the tax system to benefit themselves. As a result, the economic burden of the war is mainly placed on the heads of the general poor people, making the general people more impoverished. In this way, it can be seen that the problem of "people's burden capacity" is not only a simple economic problem, but is related to fundamental social problems.

In addition to Fried, the German pacifist Lussbinert is also a noteworthy "latent military power theorist." Like Fried, he started from the nature of future wars and first pointed out the characteristics of this war: "The distinction between combatants and non-combatants will disappear, and the front will not be the firing line of the opposing armies, but the organic whole of the entire country, the contention of the tertiary mobilization of the entire national economic organization." Needless to say, this also mainly interprets "latent military power" as economic latent power.

However, in detail, Lussbinert believed that "latent military power" is composed of the following elements: 1. "Spiritual factors, namely military capabilities, inventiveness, such as the political foresight to conclude alliances." 2. "Biological factors, namely residents, agriculture (including livestock), fuel resources, and raw materials for the textile industry." 3. "Mineralogical factors, namely undeveloped resources such as coal, iron ore, petroleum, special metals, and raw materials for the chemical industry, and mineral fertilizers." 4. "Industrial factors, namely transportation and transportation means, machinery manufacturing industry, water sources for making mechanical power or electricity sources, hydropower, and others."

In this way, the elements of "latent military power" as explained by Lussbinert are somewhat different from those of Fried, that is, the former puts certain political elements into the so-called "latent military power." For example, the "spiritual factors" he cited can be said to be certain political factors. But unfortunately, he narrowed the problem. He only saw the importance of political foresight and the ability to conclude alliances, but did not think of the more important issues of social systems and political forms. What is even more ridiculous is that he actually cited "inventiveness" as a decisive factor, masking the particularly important points of the problem. Therefore, his "latent military power theory" ultimately still takes economic latent power as the determining factor.

Lussbinert especially emphasized the importance of metals and , believing that this has the greatest determining role. Based on this view, he

Page 20

explained many famous wars of the past. He believed that in the war between Austria and Prussia, Prussia won only because it had a large amount of pig iron production; the reason for Germany's victory in the Franco-Prussian War was the same; as for the American Civil War, in his opinion, the North had abundant coal and metal, so it defeated the agricultural South; afterwards, he further said, based on this , that in the World War of 1914-18, Germany's victory over Russia was due to its greater industrial power; but because its industrial power was not as good as that of Britain and the United States, it finally failed. Thus - he concluded: "In future wars, those who have the best and most abundant raw material resources and the best methods and means of producing war machines will surely win." However, unfortunately, in explaining an important war in the past, he forgot the war in which the capitalist countries of the world besieged the Soviet Union in 1918-20; according to Lussbinert's explanation, the use of the natural wealth and industrial power of the capitalist world to attack the nascent Soviet Union would inevitably be a success and achieve a complete victory, but the result was unexpectedly that the interventionist troops of the great powers retreated in defeat. This incident was a difficult problem that Lussbinert's "latent military power theory" encountered in the course of its theoretical development and could not explain, so he simply abandoned it deliberately.

It is true that a country's economic power, what people call "latent military power," is quite related to war, but this must be combined with military armed forces, social systems, political forms, and the lives and thoughts of the people and soldiers to make an overall observation before it has meaning. It cannot be taken as the sole determining factor to explain the problem. For example, the current capitalist countries, although their industries are very developed and their financial resources are relatively abundant, are very dangerous in the process of war because the contradictions among the people in the country are becoming increasingly acute and the thoughts and actions of the people and even the army are not unified. In this way, if the people and nations oppressed by them can consistently to the end, they will surely win the final victory. According to the theory of the "latent military power theorists" mentioned above, the victor of future wars must be a country with highly developed industry, abundant raw materials, and abundant financial resources, then imperialists like the United States will inevitably win, as for the weak and small nations in the poor and weak colonies and semi-colonies and the general poor people, they will never be able to turn themselves over. This is really the view of the rich and powerful imperialism!

In fact, the "latent military power theory" mentioned above is produced by the great powers in the struggle of "disarmament" and "expansion of armaments". For example, in the past, in order to oppose Germany's expansion of armaments, Briand Ren especially attracted people's attention to the development of German industry and pointed out the power of this "latent military power". Also, when true pacifists put forward the proposition of complete disarmament, the great powers became panicked and immediately used the "latent military power theory" to deal with it, saying that the "latent military power" of various countries' chemical industry, automobile industry, machinery industry, etc. cannot be eliminated, so complete disarmament is impossible. - It is not surprising that the so-called "latent military power theory" produced in this way has expressed the views mentioned above, right?

Confession of a Professional Woman

Female Actress 182

— A Talk by Ms. Zheng Mengxia

I am from Zhongshan County, Guangdong Province. It was originally called Xiangshan to commemorate Mr. Sun Zhongshan before being renamed Zhongshan. At the age of fifteen, my father went to Shanghai to do business, and I went to Shanghai with him. I studied at Qiming Girls' School in Xujiahui. Since I was a child, I liked to hum Peking Opera tunes and often went to the theater with my father. Moreover, I have always had a natural love for music, and records are my good friends. Counting it all up, I have been fascinated by the melodies and studied Peking Opera for almost fifteen years.

Looking back to when I was nineteen, I made a guest appearance at the old Grand Stage on Sanma Road in Shanghai. That was my first public performance of Peking Opera. After that, I often performed in private gatherings. I have joined famous amateur Peking Opera troupes in Shanghai such as "Shenshang," "Zhengyi Society," and "Jingwu Athletic Association Peking Opera Department."

In 1934, I organized my own Shanghai Wanlian Opera Troupe and went south to perform at the Queen's Theatre in Hong Kong, the Xinhua Theatre in Guangzhou, and other theaters. When forming the troupe, I received help from my second husband, Mr. Guan Hongbin; and in Hong Kong and Guangdong, I also received support from friends and various sectors. However, my goal was not to make money; so although each ticket was once sold for more than three yuan and three jiao, I did not actually make much profit. In addition to performing Peking Opera, I also performed dancing with Mr. Chen Gaocong, which was relatively more popular.

Before going south, perhaps it was a coincidence? At the China National Dancing Competition organized by the Victory Radio Company, Mr. Chen Gaocong and I danced together. He was selected as the "Dancing King" of China; and I was unexpectedly selected as the "Dancing Queen." My intention was to continue to improve my skills, so I often invited famous European and American dance artists to give guidance. The same was true for Peking Opera.

My first teacher of Peking Opera, whose great name is Chen Xiangyun, was none other than Xiao Xixi, an old opera performer with great influence in the court of Empress Dowager Cixi of the Qing Dynasty. Later, I also studied under Mr. Guan Hongbin. It was Mr. Guan who introduced me to join the Shenshang amateur troupe.

I was not a child actor who started learning opera from a young age; I am considered an amateur who entered the profession. Therefore, I am not very familiar with the life of child actors. Generally speaking, if someone is naturally dull and forced to learn opera, and they encounter a teacher with a bad temper, they may inevitably suffer scolding and whipping. As for me? I can be considered a very comfortable and fortunate person. Most of the people I interact with are amateurs, and I can learn a lot just by being around them. In the past, Mr. Chen was good at elegant and martial Qingyi (virtuous female roles) and Huashan (vivacious female roles). Mr. Guan was proficient in all roles including Qingyi, Huashan, Sheng (male roles), Jing (painted-face male roles), and Chou (comedic roles).

Here, I might as well talk a little about the rules for learning Peking Opera and apprenticing to a teacher. According to the old rules, one must light incense and candles and perform a kneeling ceremony. Moreover, every time one goes on stage, one must also perform a kneeling ceremony in front of the ancestral master's seat backstage. Usually, one only needs to prepare a "guan shu" (apprenticeship contract) and bow three times to the teacher, but one must still kowtow in front of the ancestral master's seat backstage to show respect. When sending the "guan shu," one must find an introducer and a witness to sign and affix their seals. The content of the "guan shu" is roughly as follows: "The person establishing this apprenticeship contract, ××× (stating age and birthday), hereby entrusts ××× to introduce them and, after discussing the matter on three sides, voluntarily apprentices to Mr. ××× to learn opera (stating how the performance fees earned within a certain number of years will be split. After the term is over, ××× will personally take them back, etc.)."

I am truly particularly interested in Peking Opera. I think that the old plays that are very meaningful and that I have worked hard to learn include "Hongluanxi," "Huatian Cuo," "Hongniguan," and "Fengyang Flower Drum," etc. But what I find very incomprehensible is that the more effort I put into practicing the old plays, the fewer people welcome them. Therefore, on several occasions, I have had to rely on my Westernized dancing on the Peking Opera stage.

I have been to Beijing and Tianjin. I performed at the Beiyang Theatre in Tianjin, and the box office was good. I partnered with Mr. Ye Shenglan at the Huale Theatre in Beijing. The "Shi Bao" and "Li Yan Bao" newspapers in Beijing have given me a lot of guidance, encouragement, and praise. But I feel that, in my current environment, it is difficult to live up to everyone's expectations.

Unfortunately, Mr. Guan, my Qin player (musician), and several other friends who I had dealings with could not avoid taking me to court. Although it did not cause much trouble, I have gained a lot of a sense of vicissitudes because of it.

I once joined a troupe at the Tianchan Stage in Shanghai. This was because Mr. Zhao Ruquan praised my performance of "Hongluanxi," a play that I had worked hard to learn, and then contacted me. So, I feel that effort is still a necessary condition for life.

I, like a man, understand other people's psychology very well. I would not dare to say that a person is not sometimes used by others, but even if they are used, they will one day achieve their correct goal.

Book and Newspaper Review

Review of "Women's Resonance," Volume 5, Issue 4 183

— Ms. Yu Xi

—Publisher: 63 Chengxian Street, Nanjing. Price: One Dime per copy—

"Women's Resonance" is also a relatively old women's publication. I have read several issues before, but its views were not very correct. Also, the writing style was often stagnant and lacked liveliness and conciseness. Recently, I heard that the editor had been changed and that some reorganization and improvement had been made, so I bought it to read again. The one I read was Volume 5, Issue 4.

Judging solely from the articles I read, both the viewpoints and the writing techniques have indeed improved compared to the past. In some respects, it can even be said to be a progressive publication. The arrangement of the articles is relatively harmonious, because it has not fallen into the error of many previous women's publications, which only talked about partial women's issues in a self-enclosed way and forgot about politics. Even when discussing women's issues, it is able to politicize them to a considerable extent, pointing out the path to liberation for women and the path to participating in actual political struggles. For example, the articles "Rumors of a Secret Sino-Soviet Pact," "The Atmosphere of War and the Smoke Screen of War," and "Bringing All of China Together" are purely commentaries on political issues, while the essays "The Line of the Women's Movement in Extraordinary Times" and "Review of the National Assembly Representative Issue" have also politicized women's issues to a considerable extent, pointing out how the women's movement should actually participate in political activities and the line of its activities. Even the article "The Misfortune of Working Women and its Solution" has an indication of a general social and political way out. It is very correct to be able to discuss women's issues without being far from politics. In addition to these texts, there are also historical materials, descriptions of women's lives, and literary and artistic works, which also show that it is not monotonous and dry. Generally speaking, the writing style is also somewhat interesting, concise, and lively, which is also worth mentioning incidentally.

Nevertheless, it also has many shortcomings. The first thing we want to say is that some of the essays do not have a sufficiently firm and correct political stance. Therefore, when instructing women on how to engage in political struggle and lead a political life, they lack a certain social class perspective and give some incorrect route instructions. For example, the translated article "Women's Career—Politics" was written by the wife of the highest ruler of the United States, Roosevelt. What is the intention of taking the preaching of the imperialists and using it to educate one's own oppressed female masses? Moreover, the content of her article does not have any thought of resisting reality or transforming reality (of course, she would not have such thoughts). What she teaches women is only to tell them how to follow the existing rules step by step and carefully to raise their individual status and learn to be female politicians. Is this the guidance given to the women's liberation movement? Isn't this female politician clearly telling women to obey the current system and be good public servants, "loyal, courageous, and humble" public servants? If "Women's Resonance" wants to transform itself into a progressive publication at the forefront of the times, it should never publish such articles and use them to guide women's political lives.

Secondly, in this issue of "Women's Resonance," some articles with idealistic viewpoints are clearly mixed in. For example, the article "Women in the Eyes of Philosophers and Poets" completely attributes the reasons why those so-called philosophers and poets who despise women despise women to "feelings of inner guilt" and "jealous self-interest," etc., and seeks explanations from their personal relationships with women, rather than explaining how the social system and economic relations determine the reasons why these people inevitably despise women. This is an idealistic argument. Because if it is said that their opposition to women only stems from personal psychological feelings, for example, Confucius and Jesus opposed women because they hated their mothers for being unchaste, then why did all men in primitive society not have this psychology? At that time, the general children did not know who their father was, so why did the men at that time not despise their mothers? It is clear that the changes in social and economic relations and the social system formed a male-centered social consciousness, which determined these individual thoughts, and then they inevitably opposed women under the support of this social system, which was not dominated and produced by their personal psychological effects and feelings.

In addition, in this issue of the publication, the viewpoints of some articles are slightly expressed with a somewhat feminist color. Although this color is not very strong, a very progressive women's publication should completely eliminate this shortcoming. However, this issue of the publication cannot completely do so, and there is a tendency to simply oppose all men from the standpoint of women. For example, in the article "Women in the Eyes of Philosophers and Poets," because he does not look for the root cause of men's contempt for women from objective social changes, he says that there are only one in a million exceptions, and that there is not a single man who does not oppose women. In fact, as society has progressed to the present, all progressive elements of society and the broad masses of hard-working people, from the overall consciousness and tendency of his entire class, sympathize with women. Those men who stubbornly hold male-centered ideas are a minority of individuals, not an entire class, and there are many such people among women. The author may hate all men under the influence of a women-centered ideology, forgetting this fact. Another example is the article "Asking Ms. Chen Hengzhe for Advice on Surnames After Marriage." I think this small problem is not worth serious discussion. People like Chen Hengzhe and this kind of argument only need a small amount of sarcasm, and there is no need to discuss these trivial issues in a big way. Because if we argue about this issue so seriously, even if we can expose some facts of male-centered thinking, fully expressing that women must fight for the hereditary surnames of the patriarchal society is as meaningless and unreasonable as men in a male-centered society must maintain male surnames. In fact, it is wrong for men to insist that women take their surnames, as if they are treating women as their own possessions, and it is also the same mistake that women must fight for this right as men in the past. Moreover, women must fight to preserve their surnames, which does not mean that they have won any women's rights. In my opinion, men should not force women to take their surnames, as if they were treating women as their own property, but women do not necessarily have to preserve their surnames, even if they have women's rights. If this is the case, it is tantamount to treating the surnames of the patriarchal society as very precious, or to indicate that they must adhere to the position of women to confront men. This kind of thinking is backward and has a feminist color. People's names can be taken casually, so they can be taken as they please. If a woman takes any word from the man's surname or name as her own name in order to express her love for her man, as long as she is not forced to do so, there is no meaning of being insulted and despised, and it is possible. Conversely, if a man takes any word from the woman's name as his own name because he loves his woman very much, he will not be insulted and despised in the same way, and it is still possible. Such things are already very popular in modern society. If we discuss this issue as a big issue, this just shows that we must adhere to everything of women, regardless of whether it should be adhered to, and whether it is related to the real interests of women's liberation, which is a narrow feminist view.

I read this issue of "Women's Resonance," and I came up with so much criticism, but it is not to tell readers not to read it. In fact, in terms of its overall trend, it is still relatively progressive among women's publications. The general expression of dissatisfaction with reality and the general resistance of the dark side of society is still available. Even though it is slightly expressed with some women-centered thinking, this is the natural expression of the angry emotions of women who have been oppressed for thousands of years, and we should also forgive them to a considerable extent. However, for the sake of cherishing the publication, I hope that it will take another step forward in spirit and advocacy, completely eliminate these shortcomings, and more fully express its fighting spirit and correct theoretical viewpoints.

Customs and Traditions

Customs of the British Parliament 184

— Wei Quan

Everyone knows that Britain was the first country to experience the Industrial Revolution and is the home of parliamentary politics, but judging from its social system, customs, and everything else, it can be said to be the most conservative country. The so-called "Old Britain" is a general indication of its conservatism. Such conservatism can also be seen in its parliament.

First, Britain still has an emperor. When the parliament holds its opening ceremony, the King and Queen of England take a carriage decorated with gold and glass to the House of Lords. The nobles also come to the parliament hall wearing different gorgeous dresses and hats according to the differences in their ranks and titles. At the same time, noble ladies are also specially allowed to participate in this opening ceremony, and they wear even more gorgeous dresses inlaid with jewels. Therefore, the opening ceremony of the parliament is dazzling and grand, which is unmatched by other parliamentary political countries in the world.

Second, originally, the British parliament used a church, so many of the rituals of the church at that time are still preserved. For example, when members enter and leave the parliament hall, they must nod to the Speaker's seat to pay their respects. This can be said to be a sign of respect for the Speaker, but in fact, this situation is a ritual from the time when the parliament first used the church. Because at that time there was an image of Jesus on the altar in front of the Speaker, so members had to pay their respects to it. Now, although there is no altar and no image of Jesus, the conservative British still stubbornly retain that past ritual, so members still nod to the Speaker's seat when entering and leaving the parliament hall.

Third, there are also many differences in the situation when the House of Lords and the House of Commons meet. For example, when starting a speech, the House of Lords does not call the Speaker, but immediately calls the nobles and members of the House of Lords, but the House of Commons must first call the Speaker. Also, the Speaker of the House of Lords cannot decide the order of speakers during debates, so it often happens that two people speak at the same time. And even when the phenomenon of two people speaking at the same time occurs, the Speaker of the House of Lords has no right to decide who can speak first. This even has to be resolved by a vote of all members. However, the rights of the Speaker of the House of Commons are the same as those of the chairman of the meeting we usually see, which is the opposite of the former. Just looking at these two situations, we can say that the nobles of "Old Britain" are more "democratic" and "free" than its citizens, but at the same time, we can also say that this is a meeting hall habit inherited from the distinguished British nobles of the past.

Third, generally speaking, no matter which country it is, in a relatively grand parliament hall, all participants must take off their hats. But even now, when the British Parliament is in session, members do not take off their hats when sitting, but only take off their hats when standing up. Although this situation looks simple and unremarkable, it actually has its historical roots. Originally, when the British Parliament convened its first meeting, the participants included nobles, clergymen, and citizens. Among them, the nobles pretended to be very arrogant in order to show their superior status and did not take off their hats. And the newly emerged citizens at that time, although they opposed the nobles, also unconsciously imitated some of the airs of the nobles in order to show their gentlemanly demeanor. The above-mentioned situation in the current British Parliament is what has been conserved from the past.

Fourth, although British parliamentary politics has had hundreds of years of history, the cry of "Hearl Hearl" at the meeting is still preserved as it was at the beginning. For a motion, for the speaker's argument, whether it is warm applause, well-intentioned agreement, or angry opposition, fierce insult, and vicious satire, members express it by shouting "Hearl Hearl," only the pitch of the shout differs due to the difference in each person's tendency.

Finally, what I want to say is that when the British Parliament is in session, the famous London Big Ben will be lit up. Because in the past, when the King of England had greater power, it was very possible to violently suppress the parliament. In order to prevent such suppression, the British people installed large lights on this clock tower. If the lights are bright when the parliament is in session, the meeting is very safe. Conversely, if the lights are always dimmed, the meeting is being suppressed.

Page 21

Therefore, the citizens of London can rise up to resist. This situation was originally in the past era, but the conservative British still retain it to this day. So in London, as soon as we see the lights of the Big Ben tower bright, we know that the British Parliament is in session, without having to read the newspaper.

Commentary

On Encouraging Childbirth 185

— Ximen

According to the Taian Daily, the Soviet Union has drafted a new legal system to increase the birth rate. Among them, abortion is a crime, and mothers with eight, nine, ten, or eleven children in their families will receive subsidies from the state every year, at 2,000 rubles per child. For children beyond eleven, each child will receive 5,000 rubles. The number of kindergartens will be increased to 300, so that they can accommodate 2.4 million children. Divorce without mutual consent is prohibited. The purpose of the new legal system is to increase the Russian population to 300 million within 25 years. According to the latest population survey, the total number is only slightly more than 162 million.

On the other hand, we often see that Germany and Italy are also working hard to encourage childbirth. The government also gives special subsidies to women who have many children and uses various methods of commendation. At the same time, those men and women who have reached adulthood and have not yet married, or who divorce easily, or who have abortions at will, are punished.

Judging from the fact of encouraging childbirth, it seems that the world is very prosperous, and there is a need for more people to engage in production and work. It is not at all like there is a situation of "overpopulation" or "oversupply of labor." However, if we look at it from another perspective, we see the panic of unemployment everywhere, the overpopulation, and countless people who are displaced and die from famine and poverty every year. Comparing the birth rate and the death rate, the total population of the world is probably not only not increasing, but is actually decreasing day by day. Isn't this a very contradictory phenomenon? On the one hand, we are trying to encourage childbirth, and on the other hand, we are letting people be displaced and die. Rather than increasing reproduction on the one hand, it is better to find ways to reduce irregular deaths!

Due to Malthus's population law, many people who do not understand the laws of society, seeing that the laboring masses have many children and cannot afford to raise them, have come up with many theories of birth control, such as Mrs. Sanger. They believe that the reason why poor families cannot raise children is because they produce at will without restraint. Reproduction should be based on one's own economic conditions. That is to say, rich people can produce more and more because they have the power to support them; poor people should practice birth control, or it is best not to have children at all. Conversely, they also regard the proliferation of reproduction and the lack of birth control as the reason for not being able to support themselves, believing that control is the fundamental remedy. But what is the reality?

Let's see that the intention of Germany and Italy to encourage childbirth is to prepare for another world war. Because the experience of the First World War told them that countless imports need to be consumed in the war, and a continuous supply of population is needed. This is just like the need for a large number of shells and military supplies in the war. Therefore, their encouragement of reproduction is not for the people themselves, but for the preparation for aggression against weak nations and future wars, and preparing to rush to build a large number of flesh bombs. However, in fact, capitalism has developed to the current stage, which will only create unemployment and create wars, and it will never allow the population to increase naturally. It only reduces the import and destroys the population.

But the situation in the Soviet Union is slightly different. Judging from the situation of its domestic production, it seems that only the rise of productivity, the improvement of the living standards of workers, and the disappearance of the unemployed are seen, and because of the rapid progress of industrial production, a large number of laborers are needed. Therefore, its encouragement of reproduction is for economic development, which is the result of economic development.

Originally, the population problem is not simply a biological problem, but also a sociological problem. Under what economic system, there will be what kind of population law. It is by no means solvable by birth control, nor is it solvable by encouraging reproduction for other purposes without following the economic production situation. Rationalization of childbirth can only be achieved in a rational economic life.

Outlying Post Office Agency

Charcoal Kiln 186

— Charcoal Worker

Communication from Changhua County, Zhejiang

Since charcoal-fueled cars have been speeding along our inland highways, our countrymen have gradually begun to pay attention to the areas where charcoal is produced. Zhejiang and Jiangxi provinces are inherently mountainous and have made significant progress in road construction, so public buses running on the highways use a large amount of charcoal as fuel. The Changhua charcoal kilns described in this article, along with the neighboring area of Yuqian, are places with very high production volume.

Changhua County seat is located in the western part of Zhejiang Province, accessible by car directly from the provincial capital Hangzhou, a distance of 132 kilometers. The county is a mountainous area with little farmland. The customs of the people are hardworking and simple, and their lives are rudimentary. Farmers can only rely on the land along mountain streams for cultivation, so the yield of rice is not even sufficient for the food needs of the county. The wasteland is scattered and fragmented, making cultivation difficult. Thus, they mostly develop the mountains, and therefore farmers rely solely on collecting firewood and planting in the mountains as their only way out. Moreover, the mountain soil contains sand, and the forests and fruit trees are densely and luxuriantly layered. Among them, the raw materials for charcoal are undeniably abundant. On the mountains along the highway, pine and fir trees are the most numerous, followed by oak, maple, crape myrtle, cypress, yellow cedar, silk trees, etc. The best raw material for charcoal is oak, followed by maple and other miscellaneous trees, then pine trees. However, the combustion effect after the charcoal is made has its own merits.

Oak trees are divided into white oak, green oak, red oak, and sawleaf oak, collectively known as sawleaf oak. Among them, white oak is the best. White oak comes in large and small sizes, and the charcoal produced is called large and small Wugang charcoal. White oak is strong and heavy. When struck, it produces a metallic sound, and it sinks in water. The best charcoal is one with fine cracks in the core. Its firepower during combustion is double that of pine charcoal, so its price is also the highest. Wugang charcoal was invented by people from Quzhou and is only fourteen years old. Production is quite abundant. Huizhou and Ruichang also have high output. However, because the sales of Wugang charcoal are limited in Changhua County, its annual production only accounts for one-tenth of the total charcoal production. Green oak is called large and small green leaves. Large green leaves are stronger and heavier than small green leaves, and are the best among green charcoal. Its combustion performance is slightly inferior to Wugang charcoal, and the selling price is also slightly lower than Wugang charcoal. However, charcoal sellers do not have separate names for large and small green leaf charcoal, and they are collectively referred to as green charcoal. Red oak is the most common among oaks. There is no name for red oak charcoal. It is mostly mixed with green charcoal and miscellaneous charcoal for sale. As for the raw materials for miscellaneous charcoal, there are many varieties, such as charcoal made from yellow cedar, silk tree, maple, crape myrtle, cypress, and other trees, all of which belong to it, collectively referred to as miscellaneous charcoal. However, they are generally distinguished as large and small miscellaneous charcoal. Because the raw materials for large miscellaneous charcoal are thick and difficult to make charcoal, the kiln fire is too strong, and the charcoal becomes a block, so it is also called "rough chunk". Also, because the nature of miscellaneous trees is light and not strong, after the charcoal is made, it burns and explodes, and floats in water. It is commonly called "exploding charcoal" or "floating charcoal", and its sales are not as wide as small miscellaneous charcoal. The raw materials for small miscellaneous charcoal are selected from the best maple, silk tree, green firewood tree, etc., among miscellaneous trees. The charcoal body is thin and long, and can be used as green charcoal, so its sales are also the largest. Miscellaneous charcoal accounts for seven-tenths of the total annual production and sales. However, its selling price is calculated based on the weight of the charcoal, and is not divided into expensive or cheap due to the size of the charcoal. In the raw materials of pine charcoal, there is also cypress mixed in. Although pine charcoal also has large and small distinctions, its nature is the same. Pine charcoal is loose and easy to burn, with fierce flames, and short burning time, so it has no endurance. When cooking food, it is easily burned. It is rarely used in homes, and is mostly purchased by furnace workshops, cake shops, and tin shops. In recent years, the number of stores using pine charcoal has decreased due to business decline, so the production and consumption of pine charcoal only accounts for two-tenths of the total charcoal production.

When charcoal is sold in the market, there are seven common names: high-hat white oak charcoal (i.e., Wugang charcoal), flat-basket miscellaneous charcoal, high-hat green oak charcoal, round-bottom miscellaneous charcoal, small-basket miscellaneous charcoal, large-basket pine charcoal, small-basket pine charcoal, etc.

It takes three and a half days to burn charcoal once, and 640 catties of charcoal can be produced. With six workers, each worker gets 40 cents, for a total of $2.40 per day. For three and a half days, the total labor cost is $8.40, equivalent to 1.3 li per catty of charcoal. Each dan (small miscellaneous charcoal is 32 catties per dan) costs 41.6 cents, plus the cost of strolling, loading baskets, carrying, and transportation.

Continued on page 5

Page 22

Page 23

, totaling 20 cents, the total cost per dan is 71.6 cents, while the current selling price is only 50 cents per dan, a net loss of 21.6 cents.

Charcoal kilns are built jointly with funds raised by charcoal merchants, and the kiln workers are hired on a temporary basis. This type of small-scale capital business only requires 500 yuan of capital to set up a kiln independently. However, to set up a charcoal kiln, you must first find a suitable charcoal mountain location and sign a lease with the mountain owner. The rent for the charcoal mountain is not expensive. Within a radius of ten li, the rent for the charcoal mountain is only 70 to 100 yuan at most. However, when the mountain owner signs a contract with the charcoal merchant, the mountain owner can demand that all ancient fruit trees and timber trees on the mountain be restricted from being cut or damaged. This is mostly accepted by charcoal merchants, because cutting down large trees requires large wages and takes time. Moreover, the tree trunks with a diameter of 2.5 to 3 inches are the best raw material for charcoal. The trunk should be thin, and the nature should be strong and resilient. Large trees are not easy to refine, and after the charcoal is made, it is not durable. Therefore, charcoal merchants do not pay attention to this type of wood. As for the rent of the mountain land, although the rent value is determined by the distance from the water source on the charcoal mountain, the charcoal sales have been sluggish in recent years, and the mountain owners of charcoal mountains that are too far from the water source are even willing not to collect rent in order to attract charcoal merchants to set up kilns and burn. This is because once the trees are cut down, the mountain owner can change to planting six grains. Therefore, renting a mountain to set up a kiln is beneficial to both parties. Now the mountain owners have more active methods, building their own charcoal kilns so that charcoal merchants can purchase materials and burn them at any time. However, at least 100 dan of charcoal must be refined. The mountain owner's profit is calculated at 5 cents per dan. Therefore, the value of charcoal raw materials and land rent is very small. The most important thing is labor costs.

As for the number of charcoal kilns, Changhua County has four districts, originally divided into twelve villages. Since the second village was merged into the third village and the sixth village was merged into the seventh village, there are only ten villages in total. Except for the southern district, which is separated by a water line, the other three districts are all high mountains and forests, and charcoal raw materials can be picked up everywhere. Among them, the first, third, and twelfth villages produce the most charcoal, and the charcoal kilns are also the most numerous in these three places. In the 20th year of the Republic of China, there were more than 340 charcoal kilns, more than 160 in the 21st year, more than 130 in the 22nd year, and only more than 110 in the 23rd year. According to charcoal merchants, there may not even be 40 this year. The decline of the charcoal industry is even clearer from this.

Building a kiln must produce at least 500 dan of charcoal in order not to lose the estimated cost, and the kiln workers are unwilling to do back work. At the beginning of building a kiln, trees are first cut down to prepare for the construction of workers' houses and kiln pavilions, and then branch roads are opened up so that the felled tree branches can be pushed down these branch roads to the kiln side. Therefore, branch roads must be connected to the kiln base. After the branch roads are opened up, trees are felled on one side and charcoal kilns are built on the other. The main material for charcoal kilns is yellow mud, and wood is only used for building kiln pavilions. Each kiln takes about 20 days to complete, costing 70 to 80 yuan. However, in addition to wages, workers building kilns must also be given alcohol money. The shape of the charcoal kiln varies from place to place, with square and round shapes, while Changhua County is famous for its crucian carp back style. Most of the kiln workers are from Jinyun, and the most famous are from Quzhou. The quality of the charcoal depends entirely on the sophistication of the charcoal kiln's construction method, so the charcoal kiln is highly valued by charcoal merchants.

To make charcoal, all tree trunks or branches are first cut into lengths of two feet or more, and dried in the sun for three or four days. When the tree sap penetrates into the center, they can be pushed into the kiln for burning. When the raw material is burned one step, white smoke will come out of the two Tianmu holes set up on the kiln back of this step. When there is no white smoke, it is known that the raw material has been burned, and the two Tianmu holes are covered with mud. When all six Tianmu holes are closed, the raw material has been completely burned. This takes 24 hours of fire work, and the kiln must be sealed for half a day. When the remaining flames are about to die out, the charcoal door is opened one by one, and the charcoal is pulled out, and the remaining fire is quenched with charcoal shavings and charcoal sand. After another six hours, it can be loaded into the charcoal baskets. The work on the kiln takes three days before and after, and 20 dan of small basket charcoal can be produced. Each dan of small basket charcoal is calculated at 32 catties, for a total of 640 catties of charcoal, and the raw materials used are 4,200 catties. The remaining charcoal shavings should be dragged clean as much as possible so that the fire in the kiln can easily dissipate before the second charcoal making. The time between the two makings should be at least one day, so making charcoal is most suitable in spring and autumn.

Most of the kiln workers come from Yanzhou, Chuzhou, Taizhou, and Wenzhou. Workers from this county only account for three-tenths. As for the total number of workers, because the number of kilns is uncertain, it is not possible to investigate in detail. The most at one time was 1,900 people; the least was 1,300 people. Although there are kiln workers, knife workers, and carrying workers at the kiln, these three jobs and the kiln boss all take turns working by day, and their wages are equal. Before the 20th year of the Republic of China, the normal wage was one yuan per worker, and in the 21st year, it was still 60 to 70 cents, but now it is only 30 to 50 cents. However, the wages for carrying charcoal out of the water are still determined by hiring people at any time depending on the distance from the water source. The output is mostly transported by charcoal merchants hiring boats.

Art World

Re-Performance of Classical Drama 187

— Lin Zicong

Recently, the Chinese spoken drama movement seems to be more active. The factual manifestation is that recently not only have many new drama troupes been established, but also many famous dramas have been publicly performed. However, on the whole, most of the dramas performed recently that have attracted attention are famous ancient dramas, and very few new plays produced by modern China. For example, "Nora," "The Government Inspector," "La Dame aux Camélias," and the plays of Chekhov and Ostrovsky that are said to be publicly performed soon can all be said to be classical things. This has aroused discussions among some mechanically-minded people. As soon as their eyes see the word "ancient," their minds immediately think of the current retrograde restoration movement in China, saying: The current flourishing performance of classical dramas in China is a manifestation of the Chinese drama movement converging with the current entire restoration wave; the so-called new drama movement is already retreating! In fact? The problem is not that simple.

We know that before humanity has evolved into a kingdom of freedom, the lives of people in each era and society, although essentially different, have similarities in some places. Therefore, art that reflects human life, although subject to the constraints of the era and society, is possible for people in society to borrow artistic works produced in other eras and societies for the needs of real life. Under this possibility, there have been many revivals or reuse of artistic works from past eras in history. But this revival or reuse is not necessarily a manifestation of restoration or regression; the problem must be judged by the ideological content of the revived or reused art: If the revived or reused art is combined with the retrograde thought of the time, then the significance of this revival or reuse is regression; conversely, if it coincides with the progressive thought of the time at a certain point and has the function of promoting social progress, then it has progressive significance. Therefore, we cannot condemn the revival or reuse of art from past eras as restoration or regression without distinction. For example, the Renaissance can be said that the entire era of literary and cultural movement was reviving the ancient spirit, but we cannot say that the Renaissance movement was regressive; because this movement was used by the emerging citizens to break the darkness of the Middle Ages, and it was their expression of starting to create modern culture, which has new progressive significance. Drama is a field of art. For the revival or re-performance of dramas from past eras, of course, it is also necessary to evaluate it based on the ideological content of the revived or re-performed dramas, and cannot be generally condemned as restoration or regression.

Based on the above principles, we can more concretely talk about the several classical dramas that have been performed in China recently. For example, "Nora" and "The Government Inspector," which are familiar to everyone, although they are old dramas from the 19th century, their performance in China has very new significance: "Nora" opposes old morality, law, and religion, and "The Government Inspector" satirizes old bureaucrats. Every Chinese person who sees it can think of the situation in China and generate new thoughts, feelings, and even new actions. In this way, if we generalize that all the classical dramas performed in China contain a restorative flavor, it is not only a mechanical formal statement, but objectively it is mixing old and new ideas together, making people unable to see clearly and hindering everyone's progress.

Naturally, the recent popularity of classical drama performances in China is not accidental, and it is indeed related to the current restorative trend; but this relationship is not "positive" but "negative." In our opinion, under the current restorative trend, nothing can be discussed except "archaeology," "restoration," and "using the ancient to negate the present," so the new great plays that are urgently needed by the objective reality simply cannot be produced, and even if they are produced, there is no possibility of public performance? Therefore, drama activists have to work hard to find in the old paper piles of foreign countries, to find the great classical dramas that coincide with new ideas at a certain point to perform. If we want to say that the current re-performance of classical dramas in China is related to the current restorative trend, then this is the relationship; therefore, we cannot interpret these two words "relationship" as "convergence," saying that this phenomenon itself is restoration.

In addition, re-performing great classical dramas that have shown the truth of a certain era has great significance in the development of art history. This is also undeniable.

However, precisely because the significance of re-performed classical dramas is mainly to be judged by their ideological content, we cannot unconditionally say that as long as it is a classical drama, it is good, and move a classical drama to the stage when we see one. Because in classical dramas, there are also some hypocritical, decadent, and regressive drugs. If those old drugs are moved to the new stage, they will spread their toxic qualities to the audience. We should stand on the position of reality and choose the classical plays with progressive significance that are needed by China today to perform.

In the current situation in China, such as Ostrovsky's "Poverty is No Crime," Ibsen's "Pillars of Society," "An Enemy of the People," and even Goethe's "Faust," Hauptmann's "Before Sunrise," "The Weavers," etc., in a conditional way, coincide with China's realistic needs at a certain point and can be re-performed. In addition, classical dramas about national liberation are even more urgently needed by China today. Drama activists should work hard to find such plays; if they cannot find suitable ones, they should compile them with historical or realistic themes. I think that the Peking opera compiled and performed by Qilin Tong: "Regret of the Late Ming Dynasty" is quite meaningful; if someone can use the historical facts of Wu Sangui colluding with the Qing army to enter the pass as a theme and compile a new spoken drama, the significance will undoubtedly be greater. As for things like "La Dame aux Camélias" that lack positive significance, I think it is better not to perform them.

Secondly, special attention should be paid to the performance. Our re-performance of classical dramas cannot mechanically treat them as classical things and move them to the stage; but should stand on the position of reality and perform them critically and realistically. Recently, the Japanese New Cooperative Theater performed "Faust." The translator of the play, Mr. Kubo Sakae, attempted: "To re-examine classical literature with a realistic Italian method, and to give the poet Goethe a modern evaluation." He said: "Faust and Mephistopheles are not an abstract contrast between good and evil, but express two different forms of resistance to feudal society through the dramatic behavior of these two people" (see the 18th issue of "Study Abroad News"). From this, they have worked hard to make the performance of "Faust" have great practical significance. I think that all performances of classical dramas with new significance should work hard on this point. When necessary, we can even considerably change some scenes, situations, and dialogues in the play, and even place names and personal names, to make it more suitable for the current situation and needs of China, to strengthen its practical significance and value; naturally, this change must be carried out without harming the original meaning of the work and its artistic value. We also oppose changing great classical plays indiscriminately in the name of "practical significance," making them vulgar things to insult the author and fool the audience!

China Dance Academy Adds Evening Classes 189

The China Dance Academy, next to the Paris Grand Theater on Avenue Joffre in this city, is organized by dance experts. Since its establishment, it has been teaching various standard social dances for ten years. Its purpose is pure and its achievements are excellent. It has a good reputation. Recently, due to the crowding of students, evening classes have been added, from 2 pm to 10 pm every day. The tuition fee is three yuan. The regulations can be obtained.
